id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n\n\n</p>\n<table class="infobox vcard plainlist" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: #b0c4de"><span class="fn org">The Who</span></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/File:Who_-_1975.jpg" class="image" title="The Who on stage, standing and waving to a crowd"><img alt="The Who on stage, standing and waving to a crowd" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Who_-_1975.jpg/289px-Who_-_1975.jpg" width="289" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Who_-_1975.jpg/433px-Who_-_1975.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Who_-_1975.jpg/578px-Who_-_1975.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2472" data-file-height="1712" /></a><div>The Who, 1975<br />Left to right: <a href="/wiki/Roger_Daltrey" title="Roger Daltrey">Roger Daltrey</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lead_vocalist" title="Lead vocalist">vocals</a>), <a href="/wiki/John_Entwistle" title="John Entwistle">John Entwistle</a> (bass), <a href="/wiki/Keith_Moon" title="Keith Moon">Keith Moon</a> (drums), <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a> (guitar)</div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #b0c4de">Background information</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap">Also known as</span></th><td class="nickname">\n<div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li>The Detours</li>\n<li>The High Numbers</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Origin</th><td>\nLondon, England</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Genres</th><td>\n<div class="hlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rock_music" pop</a></span></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap">Years active</span></th><td>\n<div class="hlist">\n<ul><li>1964\xe2\x80\x931983</li>\n<li>1989</li>\n<li>1996\xe2\x80\x93present<br /><small>(one-off reunions: 1985, 1988, 1990, 1991, 1994)</small></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Labels</th><td>\n<div class="hlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Records" title="Brunswick Records">Brunswick</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Reaction_Records" title="Reaction Records">Reaction</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Track_Records" title="Track Records">Track</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Polydor_Records" title="Polydor Records">Polydor</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Decca_Records" title="Decca Records">Decca</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Records" title="Virgin Records">Virgin</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/MCA_Records" title="MCA Records">MCA</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros.</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Universal_Republic_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Republic Records">Universal Republic</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Atco_Records" title="Atco Records">Atco</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://thewho.com">thewho<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #b0c4de"></th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Members</th><td>\n<div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Roger_Daltrey" title="Roger Daltrey">Roger Daltrey</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #b0c4de"></th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap">Past members</span></th><td>\n<div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_Entwistle" title="John Entwistle">John Entwistle</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Doug_Sandom" title="Doug Sandom">Doug Sandom</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Keith_Moon" title="Keith Moon">Keith Moon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kenney_Jones" title="Kenney Jones">Kenney Jones</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>The Who</b> are an English <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> band formed in 1964. Their classic line-up consisted of lead singer <a href="/wiki/Roger_Daltrey" title="Roger Daltrey">Roger Daltrey</a>, guitarist and singer <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a>, bass guitarist <a href="/wiki/John_Entwistle" title="John Entwistle">John Entwistle</a>, and drummer <a href="/wiki/Keith_Moon" title="Keith Moon">Keith Moon</a>. They are considered one of the most influential rock bands of the 20th&#160;century, selling over <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">100 million records worldwide</a> and holding a reputation for their live shows and studio work.\n</p><p>The Who developed from an earlier group, the Detours, and established themselves as part of the <a href="/wiki/Pop_art" title="Pop art">pop art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mod_(subculture)" title="Mod (subculture)">mod movements</a>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Auto-destructive_art" title="Auto-destructive art">auto-destructive art</a> by <a href="/wiki/Instrument_destruction" title="Instrument destruction">destroying guitars and drums</a> on stage. Their first single as the Who, "<a href="/wiki/I_Can%27t_Explain" title="I Can&#39;t Explain">I Can\'t Explain</a>", reached the UK top&#160;ten, followed by a string of singles including "<a href="/wiki/My_Generation" title="My Generation">My Generation</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Substitute_(The_Who_song)" title="Substitute (The Who song)">Substitute</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Happy_Jack_(song)" title="Happy Jack (song)">Happy Jack</a>". In 1967, they performed at the <a href="/wiki/Monterey_Pop_Festival" title="Monterey Pop Festival">Monterey Pop Festival</a> and released the US top&#160;ten single "<a href="/wiki/I_Can_See_for_Miles" title="I Can See for Miles">I Can See for Miles</a>", while touring extensively. The group\'s fourth album, 1969\'s <a href="/wiki/Rock_opera" title="Rock opera">rock opera</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Tommy_(album)" title="Tommy (album)">Tommy</a></i>, included the single "<a href="/wiki/Pinball_Wizard" title="Pinball Wizard">Pinball Wizard</a>" and was a critical and commercial success. Live appearances at <a href="/wiki/Woodstock" title="Woodstock">Woodstock</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_Festival" title="Isle of Wight Festival">Isle of Wight Festival</a>, along with the live album <i><a href="/wiki/Live_at_Leeds" title="Live at Leeds">Live at Leeds</a></i>, cemented their reputation as a respected rock act. With their success came increased pressure on lead songwriter Townshend, and the follow-up to <i>Tommy</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lifehouse_(rock_opera)" title="Lifehouse (rock opera)">Lifehouse</a></i>, was abandoned. Songs from the project made up 1971\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Who%27s_Next" title="Who&#39;s Next">Who\'s Next</a></i>, which included the hit "<a href="/wiki/Won%27t_Get_Fooled_Again" title="Won&#39;t Get Fooled Again">Won\'t Get Fooled Again</a>". The group released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Quadrophenia" title="Quadrophenia">Quadrophenia</a></i> in 1973 as a celebration of their mod roots, and oversaw the <a href="/wiki/Tommy_(1975_film)" title="Tommy (1975 film)">film adaptation of <i>Tommy</i></a> in 1975. They continued to tour to large audiences before semi-retiring from live performances at the end of 1976. The release of <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Are_You" title="Who Are You">Who Are You</a></i> in 1978 was overshadowed by the death of Moon shortly after.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kenney_Jones" title="Kenney Jones">Kenney Jones</a> replaced Moon and the group resumed activity, releasing a <a href="/wiki/Quadrophenia_(film)" title="Quadrophenia (film)">film adaptation of <i>Quadrophenia</i></a> and the retrospective documentary <i><a href="/wiki/The_Kids_Are_Alright_(film)" title="The Kids Are Alright (film)">The Kids Are Alright</a></i>. After Townshend became weary of touring, the group split in 1982. The Who occasionally re-formed for live appearances such as <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> in 1985, a 25th&#160;anniversary tour in 1989 and a tour of <i>Quadrophenia</i> in 1996\xe2\x80\x931997. They resumed regular touring in 1999, with drummer <a href="/wiki/Zak_Starkey" title="Zak Starkey">Zak Starkey</a>. After Entwistle\'s death in 2002, plans for a new album were delayed. Townshend and Daltrey continued as the Who, releasing <i><a href="/wiki/Endless_Wire_(The_Who_album)" title="Endless Wire (The Who album)">Endless Wire</a></i> in 2006, and continued to play live regularly.\n</p><p>The Who\'s major contributions to rock music include the development of the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_stack" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshall stack">Marshall stack</a>, large <a href="/wiki/Public_address_system" title="Public address system">PA systems</a>, use of the synthesizer, Entwistle and Moon\'s lead playing styles, Townshend\'s feedback and power chord guitar technique, and the development of the <a href="/wiki/Rock_opera" title="Rock opera">rock opera</a>. They are cited as an influence by <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">hard rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> and mod bands, and their songs still receive regular exposure.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" class="toctext">Quadrophenia and More</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#The_Who_Hits_50!_and_beyond"><span class="tocnumber">1.5.5</span> <span class="toctext"><i>The Who Hits 50!</i> and beyond</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Musical_style_and_equipment"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Musical style and equipment</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Vocals"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Vocals</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Guitars"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Guitars</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Bass"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Bass</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Drums"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Drums</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Songwriting"><span class="tocnumber">2.5</span> <span class="toctext">Songwriting</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Personal_relationships"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Personal relationships</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Legacy_and_influence"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Legacy and influence</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Awards_and_nominations"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Awards and nominations</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Band_members"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Band members</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Current_members"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Current members</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Former_members"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Former members</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Current_touring_musicians"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Current touring musicians</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Discography"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Discography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Studio_albums"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Studio albums</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Tours_and_performances"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Tours and performances</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Headlining_1960s\xe2\x80\x931990s"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Headlining 1960s\xe2\x80\x931990s</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#Headlining_2000s\xe2\x80\x932010s"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Headlining 2000s\xe2\x80\x932010s</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-44"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TVU_Campus_St_Marys_Road.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of Ealing Art College in 2010" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/TVU_Campus_St_Marys_Road.jpg/220px-TVU_Campus_St_Marys_Road.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/TVU_Campus_St_Marys_Road.jpg/330px-TVU_Campus_St_Marys_Road.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/TVU_Campus_St_Marys_Road.jpg/440px-TVU_Campus_St_Marys_Road.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TVU_Campus_St_Marys_Road.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a> attended <a href="/wiki/Ealing_Art_College" title="Ealing Art College">Ealing Art College</a> (pictured in 2010), and his experience there contributed to The Who\'s career.</div></div></div>\n<p>The founding members of the Who, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Daltrey" title="Roger Daltrey">Roger Daltrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Entwistle" title="John Entwistle">John Entwistle</a>, grew up in <a href="/wiki/Acton,_London" title="Acton, London">Acton, London</a> and went to <a href="/wiki/Acton_High_School" title="Acton High School">Acton County Grammar School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198313,_19,_24_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198313,_19,_24-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Townshend\'s father, <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Townshend" title="Cliff Townshend">Cliff</a>, played saxophone and his mother, Betty, had sung in the entertainment division of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> during World War II, and both supported their son\'s interest in <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198315\xe2\x80\x9316_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198315\xe2\x80\x9316-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Townshend and Entwistle became friends in their second year of Acton County, and formed a <a href="/wiki/Trad_jazz" title="Trad jazz">trad jazz</a> group;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198326_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198326-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Entwistle also played <a href="/wiki/French_horn" title="French horn">French horn</a> in the Middlesex Schools\' Symphony Orchestra. Both were interested in rock, and Townshend particularly admired <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Richard" title="Cliff Richard">Cliff Richard</a>\'s d\xc3\xa9but single, "<a href="/wiki/Move_It" title="Move It">Move It</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200917_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200917-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Entwistle moved to guitar, but struggled with it due to his large fingers, and moved to bass on hearing the guitar work of <a href="/wiki/Duane_Eddy" title="Duane Eddy">Duane Eddy</a>. He was unable to afford a bass and built one at home.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198329_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198329-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200917_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200917-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> After Acton County, Townshend attended <a href="/wiki/Ealing_Art_College" title="Ealing Art College">Ealing Art College</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200920_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200920-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> a move he later described as profoundly influential on the course of the Who.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200922_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200922-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Daltrey, who was in the year above, had moved to Acton from <a href="/wiki/Shepherd%27s_Bush" title="Shepherd&#39;s Bush">Shepherd\'s Bush</a>, a more working-class area. He had trouble fitting in at the school, and discovered gangs and rock and roll.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198314_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198314-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He was expelled at 15 and found work on a building site.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200911_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200911-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In 1959 he started the Detours, the band that was to evolve into the Who. The band played professional gigs, such as corporate and wedding functions, and Daltrey kept a close eye on the finances as well as the music.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198331_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198331-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Daltrey spotted Entwistle by chance on the street carrying a bass and recruited him into the Detours.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200918_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200918-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In mid-1961, Entwistle suggested Townshend as a guitarist,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200918_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200918-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Daltrey on lead guitar, Entwistle on bass, Harry Wilson on drums, and Colin Dawson on vocals.  The band played instrumentals by <a href="/wiki/The_Shadows" title="The Shadows">the Shadows</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Ventures" title="The Ventures">the Ventures</a>, and a variety of pop and trad jazz covers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200919_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200919-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Daltrey was considered the leader and, according to Townshend, "ran things the way he wanted them".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200922_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200922-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Wilson was fired in mid-1962 and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Doug_Sandom" title="Doug Sandom">Doug Sandom</a>, though he was older than the rest of the band, married, and a more proficient musician, having been playing semi-professionally for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200919\xe2\x80\x9320_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200919\xe2\x80\x9320-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dawson left after frequently arguing with Daltrey<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200922_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200922-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and after being briefly replaced by Gabby Connolly, Daltrey moved to lead vocals. Townshend, with Entwistle\'s encouragement, became the sole guitarist. Through Townshend\'s mother, the group obtained a management contract with local promoter Robert Druce,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200921_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200921-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> who started booking the band as a support act. The Detours were influenced by the bands they supported, including <a href="/wiki/Screaming_Lord_Sutch" title="Screaming Lord Sutch">Screaming Lord Sutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Bennett_and_the_Rebel_Rousers" title="Cliff Bennett and the Rebel Rousers">Cliff Bennett and the Rebel Rousers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shane_Fenton_and_the_Fentones" title="Shane Fenton and the Fentones">Shane Fenton and the Fentones</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Kidd_and_the_Pirates" class="mw-redirect" title="Johnny Kidd and the Pirates">Johnny Kidd and the Pirates</a>. The Detours were particularly interested in the Pirates as they also only had one guitarist, <a href="/wiki/Mick_Green" title="Mick Green">Mick Green</a>, who inspired Townshend to combine rhythm and lead guitar in his style.  Entwistle\'s bass became more of a lead instrument,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200924_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200924-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> playing melodies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAtkins200065_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAtkins200065-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In February 1964, the Detours became aware of the group Johnny Devlin and the Detours and changed their name.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200926_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200926-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Townshend and his roommate Richard Barnes spent a night considering names, focusing on a theme of joke announcements, including "No One" and "the Group". Townshend preferred "the Hair", and Barnes liked "the Who" because it "had a pop punch".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198365_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198365-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Daltrey chose "the Who" the next morning.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198366_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198366-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1964.E2.80.931978"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1964\xe2\x80\x931978">1964\xe2\x80\x931978</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h4>\n<p>By the time the Detours had become the Who, they had already found regular gigs, including at the Oldfield Hotel in Greenford, the White Hart Hotel in Acton, the Goldhawk Social Club in Shepherd\'s Bush, and the Notre Dame Hall in Leicester Square.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher199868_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher199868-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> They had also replaced Druce as manager with Helmut Gorden, with whom they secured an audition with Chris Parmeinter for <a href="/wiki/Fontana_Records" title="Fontana Records">Fontana Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher199870_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher199870-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Parmeinter found problems with the drumming and, according to Sandom, Townshend immediately turned on him and threatened to fire him if his playing did not immediately improve. Sandom left in disgust, but was persuaded to lend his kit to any potential stand-ins or replacements. Sandom and Townshend did not speak to each other again for 14 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198378\xe2\x80\x9379_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198378\xe2\x80\x9379-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During a gig with a stand-in drummer in late April at the Oldfield, the band first met Keith Moon. Moon grew up in <a href="/wiki/Wembley" title="Wembley">Wembley</a>, and had been drumming in bands since 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher199829_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher199829-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He was performing with a semi-professional band called the Beachcombers, and wanted to play full-time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198380_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198380-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Moon played a few songs with the group, breaking a bass drum pedal and tearing a drum skin. The band were impressed with his energy and enthusiasm, and offered him the job.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher199873_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher199873-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Moon performed with the Beachcombers a few more times, but dates clashed and he chose to devote himself to the Who. The Beachcombers auditioned Sandom, but were unimpressed and did not ask him to join.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher199880\xe2\x80\x9381_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher199880\xe2\x80\x9381-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Who changed managers to <a href="/wiki/Peter_Meaden" title="Peter Meaden">Peter Meaden</a>. He decided that the group would be ideal to represent the growing <a href="/wiki/Mod_(subculture)" title="Mod (subculture)">mod</a> movement in Britain which involved fashion, <a href="/wiki/Scooter_(motorcycle)" title="Scooter (motorcycle)">scooters</a> and music genres such as <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">rhythm and blues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beat_music" title="Beat music">beat</a>. He renamed the group the High Numbers, dressed them up in mod clothes,<sup id="cite_ref-eder_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eder-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> secured a second, more favourable audition with Fontana and wrote the lyrics for both sides of their single "<a href="/wiki/Zoot_Suit/I%27m_the_Face" title="Zoot Suit/I&#39;m the Face">Zoot Suit"/"I\'m the Face</a>" to appeal to mods. The tune for "Zoot Suit" was "Misery" by the Dynamics,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and "I\'m the Face" borrowed from <a href="/wiki/Slim_Harpo" title="Slim Harpo">Slim Harpo</a>\'s "I Got Love If You Want It".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher199891\xe2\x80\x9392_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher199891\xe2\x80\x9392-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Although Meaden tried to promote the single, it failed to reach the top 50<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200954_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200954-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> and the band reverted to calling themselves the Who.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200960_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200960-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The group began to improve their stage image; Daltrey started using his microphone cable as a <a href="/wiki/Whip" title="Whip">whip</a> on stage, and occasionally leapt into the crowd; Moon threw drumsticks into the air mid-beat; Townshend mimed machine gunning the crowd with his guitar while jumping on stage and playing guitar with a fast arm-windmilling motion,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983120_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983120-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> or stood with his arms aloft allowing his guitar to produce feedback in a posture dubbed "the Bird Man".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199444_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199444-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Meaden was replaced as manager by two filmmakers, <a href="/wiki/Kit_Lambert" title="Kit Lambert">Kit Lambert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Stamp" title="Chris Stamp">Chris Stamp</a>. They were looking for a young, unsigned rock group that they could make a film about,<sup id="cite_ref-kurutz_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kurutz-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and had seen the band at the Railway Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Wealdstone" title="Wealdstone">Wealdstone</a>, which had become a regular venue for them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200955_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200955-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Lambert related to Townshend and his art school background, and encouraged him to write songs.<sup id="cite_ref-kurutz_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kurutz-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In August, Lambert and Stamp made a promotional film featuring the group and their audience at the Railway.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200956_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200956-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The band changed their set towards soul, <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">rhythm and blues</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motown" title="Motown">Motown</a> covers, and created the slogan "Maximum R&amp;B".<sup id="cite_ref-eder_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eder-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 1964, during a performance at the Railway, Townshend accidentally broke the head of his guitar on the low ceiling of the stage.<sup id="cite_ref-Railway_Hotel_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Railway_Hotel-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Angered by the audience\'s laughter, he smashed the instrument on the stage, then picked up another guitar and continued the show. The following week, the audience were keen to see a repeat of the event. Moon obliged by kicking his drum kit over,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983125_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983125-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Auto-destructive_art" title="Auto-destructive art">auto-destructive art</a> became a feature of the Who\'s live set.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983126_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983126-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_singles_and_My_Generation">First singles and <i>My Generation</i></span></h4>\n<p>By late&#160;1964, the Who were becoming popular in London\'s <a href="/wiki/The_Marquee" class="mw-redirect" title="The Marquee">Marquee</a> club, and a rave review of their live act appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Melody_Maker" title="Melody Maker">Melody Maker</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983134_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983134-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Lambert and Stamp attracted the attention of the American producer <a href="/wiki/Shel_Talmy" title="Shel Talmy">Shel Talmy</a>, who had produced <a href="/wiki/The_Kinks" title="The Kinks">the Kinks</a>. Townshend had written a song, "<a href="/wiki/I_Can%27t_Explain" title="I Can&#39;t Explain">I Can\'t Explain</a>", that deliberately sounded like the Kinks to attract Talmy\'s attention. Talmy saw the group in rehearsals and was impressed. He signed them to his production company,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward2004106\xe2\x80\x93107_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward2004106\xe2\x80\x93107-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and sold the recording to the US arm of <a href="/wiki/Decca_Records" title="Decca Records">Decca Records</a>, which meant that the group\'s early singles were released in Britain on <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Records" title="Brunswick Records">Brunswick Records</a>, one of UK Decca\'s labels for US artists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983151\xe2\x80\x93152_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983151\xe2\x80\x93152-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> "I Can\'t Explain" was recorded in early November 1964 at Pye Studios in <a href="/wiki/Marble_Arch" title="Marble Arch">Marble Arch</a> with <a href="/wiki/The_Ivy_League_(band)" title="The Ivy League (band)">the Ivy League</a> on backing vocals, and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">Jimmy Page</a> played <a href="/wiki/Fuzz_guitar" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuzz guitar">fuzz guitar</a> on the B-side, "Bald Headed Woman".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200960_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200960-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>"I Can\'t Explain" became popular with <a href="/wiki/Pirate_radio_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Pirate radio in the United Kingdom">pirate radio</a> stations such as <a href="/wiki/Radio_Caroline" title="Radio Caroline">Radio Caroline</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983152_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983152-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Pirate radio was important for bands as there were no commercial radio stations in the UK and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio" title="BBC Radio">BBC Radio</a> played little pop music.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983100_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983100-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The group gained further exposure when they appeared on the television programme <i><a href="/wiki/Ready_Steady_Go!" title="Ready Steady Go!">Ready Steady Go!</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-eder_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eder-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Lambert and Stamp were tasked with finding "typical teens", and invited the group\'s regular audience from the Goldhawk Social Club.<sup id="cite_ref-carr_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carr-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Enthusiastic reception on television and regular airplay on pirate radio helped the single slowly climb the charts in early 1965 until it reached the top 10.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009419_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009419-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The follow-up single, "<a href="/wiki/Anyway,_Anyhow,_Anywhere" title="Anyway, Anyhow, Anywhere">Anyway, Anyhow, Anywhere</a>", by Townshend and Daltrey,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward2004107\xe2\x80\x93108_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward2004107\xe2\x80\x93108-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> features guitar noises such as <a href="/wiki/Pick_slide" title="Pick slide">pick sliding</a>, toggle switching<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAledort199458_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAledort199458-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Audio_feedback" title="Audio feedback">feedback</a>, which was so unconventional that it was initially rejected by the US arm of Decca. The single reached the top&#160;10 in the UK<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward2004107\xe2\x80\x93108_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward2004107\xe2\x80\x93108-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and was used as the theme song to <i>Ready Steady Go!</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAledort199457_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAledort199457-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The transition to a hit-making band with original material, encouraged by Lambert, did not sit well with Daltrey, and a recording session of R&amp;B covers went unreleased.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998121_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998121-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The Who were not close friends either, apart from Moon and Entwistle, who enjoyed visiting nightclubs together in the <a href="/wiki/West_End_of_London" title="West End of London">West End of London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998126_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998126-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The group experienced a difficult time when touring Denmark in September, which culminated in Daltrey throwing Moon\'s <a href="/wiki/Amphetamine" title="Amphetamine">amphetamines</a> down the toilet and assaulting him. Immediately on returning to Britain, Daltrey was sacked,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200993_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200993-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> but was reinstated on the condition that the group became a democracy without his dominant leadership. At this time, the group enlisted <a href="/wiki/Richard_Cole" title="Richard Cole">Richard Cole</a> as a roadie.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998130\xe2\x80\x93132_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998130\xe2\x80\x93132-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">\n<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:My_Generation_sample.ogg" title="File:My Generation sample.ogg">Brief sample from the song "My Generation"</a></div>\n<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="18.018684807256" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="My_Generation_sample.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b1/My_Generation_sample.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (84 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="83672" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/b/b1/My_Generation_sample.ogg/My_Generation_sample.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="224352" /></audio></div></div>\n<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">"My Generation" includes the line "Hope I die before I get old".</div></div></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The next single, "<a href="/wiki/My_Generation" title="My Generation">My Generation</a>", followed in October. Townshend had written it as a slow blues, but after several abortive attempts, it was turned into a more powerful song with a bass solo from Entwistle. The song used gimmicks such as a vocal <a href="/wiki/Stutter" class="mw-redirect" title="Stutter">stutter</a> to simulate the speech of a mod on <a href="/wiki/Substituted_amphetamine" title="Substituted amphetamine">amphetamines</a>, and two <a href="/wiki/Modulation_(music)" title="Modulation (music)">key changes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983182_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983182-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Townshend insisted in interviews that the lyrics "Hope I die before I get old" were not meant to be taken literally.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998x_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998x-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Peaking at No.&#160;2, "My Generation" is the group\'s highest-charting single in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009419_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009419-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The d\xc3\xa9but album <i>My Generation</i> was released in late 1965. Among original material by Townshend, including the title track and "<a href="/wiki/The_Kids_Are_Alright_(song)" title="The Kids Are Alright (song)">The Kids Are Alright</a>", the album has several <a href="/wiki/James_Brown" title="James Brown">James Brown</a> covers from the session earlier that year that Daltrey favoured.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After <i>My Generation</i>, the Who fell out with Talmy, which meant an abrupt end to their recording contract. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983199_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983199-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The resulting legal acrimony resulted in Talmy holding the rights to the master tapes, which prevented the album from being reissued until 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward2004108_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward2004108-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The Who were signed to <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stigwood" title="Robert Stigwood">Robert Stigwood</a>\'s label, Reaction, and released "<a href="/wiki/Substitute_(The_Who_song)" title="Substitute (The Who song)">Substitute</a>". Townshend said he wrote the song about identity crisis, and as a parody of <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">the Rolling Stones</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/19th_Nervous_Breakdown" title="19th Nervous Breakdown">19th Nervous Breakdown</a>". It was the first single to feature him playing an acoustic <a href="/wiki/Twelve-string_guitar" title="Twelve-string guitar">twelve-string guitar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983200\xe2\x80\x93201_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983200\xe2\x80\x93201-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Talmy took legal action over the B-side, "Instant Party", and the single was withdrawn. A new B-side, "Waltz for a Pig", was recorded by the <a href="/wiki/Graham_Bond" title="Graham Bond">Graham Bond Organisation</a> under the pseudonym "the Who Orchestra".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983203_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983203-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1966 the Who released "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_a_Boy" title="I&#39;m a Boy">I\'m a Boy</a>", about a boy dressed as a girl, taken from an abortive collection of songs called <i>Quads</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983217_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983217-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Happy_Jack_(song)" title="Happy Jack (song)">Happy Jack</a>";<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009109_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009109-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and an EP, <i><a href="/wiki/Ready_Steady_Who" title="Ready Steady Who">Ready Steady Who</a></i>, that tied in with their regular appearances on <i>Ready Steady Go!</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983218_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983218-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The group continued to have conflict; on 20 May, Moon and Entwistle were late to a gig having been on the <i>Ready Steady Go!</i> set with <a href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys" title="The Beach Boys">The Beach Boys</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Johnston" title="Bruce Johnston">Bruce Johnston</a>. During "My Generation", Townshend attacked Moon with his guitar; Moon suffered a black eye and bruises, and he and Entwistle left the band, but changed their minds and rejoined a week later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998160_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998160-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Moon kept looking for other work, and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a> had him play drums on his song "<a href="/wiki/Beck%27s_Bolero" title="Beck&#39;s Bolero">Beck\'s Bolero</a>" (with Page, <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones_(musician)" title="John Paul Jones (musician)">John Paul Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicky_Hopkins" title="Nicky Hopkins">Nicky Hopkins</a>) because he was "trying to get Keith out of the Who".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998175_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998175-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="A_Quick_One_and_The_Who_Sell_Out"><i>A Quick One</i> and <i>The Who Sell Out</i></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roger_Daltrey_-left_and_Keith_Moon-right_1967.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Roger Daltrey and Keith Moon backstage in 1967" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Roger_Daltrey_-left_and_Keith_Moon-right_1967.jpg/220px-Roger_Daltrey_-left_and_Keith_Moon-right_1967.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Roger_Daltrey_-left_and_Keith_Moon-right_1967.jpg/330px-Roger_Daltrey_-left_and_Keith_Moon-right_1967.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Roger_Daltrey_-left_and_Keith_Moon-right_1967.jpg/440px-Roger_Daltrey_-left_and_Keith_Moon-right_1967.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1298" data-file-height="920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roger_Daltrey_-left_and_Keith_Moon-right_1967.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roger Daltrey (left) and Keith Moon, 1967</div></div></div>\n<p>To alleviate financial pressure on the band, Lambert arranged a song-writing deal which required each member to write two songs for the next album. Entwistle contributed "<a href="/wiki/Boris_the_Spider" title="Boris the Spider">Boris the Spider</a>" and "Whiskey Man" and found a niche role as second songwriter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983225_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983225-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The band found they needed to fill an extra ten minutes, and Lambert encouraged Townshend to write a longer piece, "<a href="/wiki/A_Quick_One,_While_He%27s_Away" title="A Quick One, While He&#39;s Away">A Quick One, While He\'s Away</a>". The suite of song fragments is about a girl who has an affair while her lover is away, but is ultimately forgiven. The album was titled <i>A Quick One</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983227_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983227-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> (<i>Happy Jack</i> in the US),<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and reached No.&#160;4 in the UK charts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983229_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983229-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> It was followed in 1967 by the UK Top 5 single "<a href="/wiki/Pictures_of_Lily" title="Pictures of Lily">Pictures of Lily</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009420_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009420-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 1966, <i>Ready Steady Go!</i> had ended, the mod movement was becoming unfashionable, and the Who found themselves in competition on the London circuit with groups including <a href="/wiki/Cream_(band)" title="Cream (band)">Cream</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Jimi_Hendrix_Experience" title="The Jimi Hendrix Experience">the Jimi Hendrix Experience</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983239\xe2\x80\x93240_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983239\xe2\x80\x93240-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Lambert and Stamp realised that commercial success in the US was paramount to the group\'s future, and arranged a deal with promoter <a href="/wiki/Frank_Barsalona" title="Frank Barsalona">Frank Barsalona</a> for a short package tour in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983243_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983243-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The group\'s performances, which still involved smashing guitars and kicking over drums, were well received,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983247_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983247-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> and led to their first major US appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Monterey_Pop_Festival" title="Monterey Pop Festival">Monterey Pop Festival</a>. The group, especially Moon, were not fond of the <a href="/wiki/Hippie" title="Hippie">hippie</a> movement, and thought their violent stage act would stand in sharp contrast to the peaceful atmosphere of the festival. Hendrix was also on the bill, and was also going to smash his guitar on stage. Townshend verbally abused Hendrix and accused him of stealing his act,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998188_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998188-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and the pair argued about who should go on stage first, with the Who winning the argument.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcMichaelLyons1998223_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcMichaelLyons1998223-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The Who brought hired equipment to the festival; Hendrix shipped over his regular touring gear from Britain, including a full <a href="/wiki/Marshall_stack" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshall stack">Marshall stack</a>. According to biographer <a href="/wiki/Tony_Fletcher" title="Tony Fletcher">Tony Fletcher</a>, Hendrix sounded "so much better than the Who it was embarrassing".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998189_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998189-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The Who\'s appearance at Monterey gave them recognition in the US, and "Happy Jack" reached the top 30.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998189_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998189-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The group followed Monterey with a US tour supporting <a href="/wiki/Herman%27s_Hermits" title="Herman&#39;s Hermits">Herman\'s Hermits</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998189_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998189-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The Hermits were a straightforward pop band and enjoyed drugs and practical jokes. They bonded with Moon,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998193_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998193-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> who was excited to learn that <a href="/wiki/Cherry_bomb" title="Cherry bomb">cherry bombs</a> were legal to purchase in Alabama. Moon acquired a reputation of destroying hotel rooms while on tour,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983247_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983247-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> with a particular interest in blowing up toilets. Entwistle said the first cherry bomb they tried "blew a hole in the suitcase <i>and</i> the chair".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998194_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998194-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Moon recalled his first attempt to flush one down the toilet: "[A]ll that porcelain flying through the air was quite unforgettable. I never realised dynamite was so powerful."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998194_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998194-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> After a gig in <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">Flint, Michigan</a> on Moon\'s 21st birthday on 23 August 1967, the entourage caused $24,000 of damage at the hotel, and Moon knocked out one of his front teeth.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998197_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998197-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Daltrey later said that the tour brought the band closer, and as the support act, they could turn up and perform a short show without any major responsibilities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983266_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983266-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Entwistle_in_1967_with_The_Who.jpg" class="image"><img alt="John Entwistle backstage with a bass guitar" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/John_Entwistle_in_1967_with_The_Who.jpg/220px-John_Entwistle_in_1967_with_The_Who.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/John_Entwistle_in_1967_with_The_Who.jpg/330px-John_Entwistle_in_1967_with_The_Who.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/John_Entwistle_in_1967_with_The_Who.jpg/440px-John_Entwistle_in_1967_with_The_Who.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1308" data-file-height="910" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Entwistle_in_1967_with_The_Who.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>John Entwistle backstage in 1967</div></div></div>\n<p>After the Hermits tour, the Who recorded their next single, "<a href="/wiki/I_Can_See_for_Miles" title="I Can See for Miles">I Can See for Miles</a>", which Townshend had written in 1966 but had avoided recording until he was sure it could be produced well.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983273_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983273-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>  Townshend called it "the ultimate Who record",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009149_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009149-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> and was disappointed it reached only No.&#160;10 in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009149_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009149-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> It became their best selling single in the US, reaching No.&#160;9.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009420_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009420-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The group toured the US again with <a href="/wiki/The_Animals" title="The Animals">Eric Burdon and the Animals</a>, including an appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Smothers_Brothers_Comedy_Hour" title="The Smothers Brothers Comedy Hour">The Smothers Brothers Comedy Hour</a></i>, miming to "I Can See For Miles" and "My Generation".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983275_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983275-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Moon bribed a stage hand to put explosives in his drum kit, who loaded it with ten times the expected quantity. The resulting detonation threw Moon off his drum riser and his arm was cut by flying cymbal shrapnel. Townshend\'s hair was singed and his left ear left ringing, and a camera and studio monitor were destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983275\xe2\x80\x93276_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983275\xe2\x80\x93276-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The next album was <i><a href="/wiki/The_Who_Sell_Out" title="The Who Sell Out">The Who Sell Out</a></i>\xe2\x80\x94a <a href="/wiki/Concept_album" title="Concept album">concept album</a> paying tribute to pirate radio, which had been outlawed in August 1967 by the <a href="/wiki/Marine,_%26c.,_Broadcasting_(Offences)_Act_1967" title="Marine, &amp;c., Broadcasting (Offences) Act 1967">Marine, &amp;c., Broadcasting (Offences) Act 1967</a>. It included humorous jingles and mock commercials between songs,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009148\xe2\x80\x93149_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009148\xe2\x80\x93149-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> a mini <a href="/wiki/Rock_opera" title="Rock opera">rock opera</a> called "Rael", and "I Can See For Miles".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009149_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009149-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The Who declared themselves a <a href="/wiki/Pop_art" title="Pop art">pop art</a> group and thus viewed advertising as an artform; they recorded a wide variety of radio advertisements, such as for canned milkshakes and the <a href="/wiki/American_Cancer_Society" title="American Cancer Society">American Cancer Society</a>, in defiance of the rising anti-consumerist ethos of the hippie counterculture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199444,_47_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199444,_47-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Townshend stated, "We don\'t change offstage. We live pop art."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200967_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200967-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Later that year, Lambert and Stamp formed a record label, <a href="/wiki/Track_Records" title="Track Records">Track Records</a>, with distribution by <a href="/wiki/Polydor" class="mw-redirect" title="Polydor">Polydor</a>. As well as signing Hendrix, Track became the imprint for all the Who\'s UK output until the mid-1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983250_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983250-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The group started 1968 by touring Australia and New Zealand with the <a href="/wiki/Small_Faces" title="Small Faces">Small Faces</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009196_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009196-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The groups had trouble with the local authorities and the <i>New Zealand Truth</i> called them "unwashed, foul-smelling, booze-swilling no-hopers".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983293_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983293-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998180_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998180-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>  They continued to tour across the US and Canada during the first half of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009190_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009190-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Tommy.2C_Woodstock_and_Live_at_Leeds"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tommy,_Woodstock_and_Live_at_Leeds"><i>Tommy</i>, Woodstock and <i>Live at Leeds</i></span></h4>\n<p>By 1968 the Who had started to attract attention in the <a href="/wiki/Underground_press" title="Underground press">underground press</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009191_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009191-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Townshend had stopped using drugs and became interested in the teachings of <a href="/wiki/Meher_Baba" title="Meher Baba">Meher Baba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983294_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983294-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In August, he gave an interview to <i>Rolling Stone</i> editor <a href="/wiki/Jann_Wenner" title="Jann Wenner">Jann Wenner</a> describing in detail the plot of a new album project and its relationship to Baba\'s teachings. The album went through several names during recording, including <i>Deaf Dumb and Blind Boy</i> and <i>Amazing Journey</i>; Townshend settled on <i><a href="/wiki/Tommy_(album)" title="Tommy (album)">Tommy</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983317_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983317-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> for the album about the life of a deaf, dumb and blind boy, and his attempt to communicate with others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983314\xe2\x80\x93315_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983314\xe2\x80\x93315-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Some songs, such as "Welcome" and "Amazing Journey" were inspired by Baba\'s teaching,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983320_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983320-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> and others came from observations within the band. "Sally Simpson" is about a fan who tried to climb on stage at a gig by <a href="/wiki/The_Doors" title="The Doors">the Doors</a> that they attended<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983316_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983316-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> and "<a href="/wiki/Pinball_Wizard" title="Pinball Wizard">Pinball Wizard</a>" was written so that <i>New York Times</i> journalist <a href="/wiki/Nik_Cohn" title="Nik Cohn">Nik Cohn</a>, a pinball enthusiast, would give the album a good review.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009221_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009221-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Townshend later said, "I wanted the story of <i>Tommy</i> to have several levels&#160;... a rock singles level and a bigger concept level", containing the spiritual message he wanted as well as being entertaining.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983318_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983318-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The album was projected for a Christmas 1968 release<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983318_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983318-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> but recording stalled after Townshend decided to make a <a href="/wiki/Double_album" title="Double album">double album</a> to cover the story in sufficient depth.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983323_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983323-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the end of the year, 18 months of touring had led to a well-rehearsed and tight live band, which was evident when they performed "A Quick One While He\'s Away" at <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones_Rock_and_Roll_Circus" title="The Rolling Stones Rock and Roll Circus">The Rolling Stones Rock and Roll Circus</a></i> television special. The Stones considered their own performance lacklustre, and the project was never broadcast.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998228\xe2\x80\x93229_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998228\xe2\x80\x93229-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The Who had not released an album in over a year, and had not completed the recording of <i>Tommy</i>, which continued well into 1969, interspersed with gigs at weekends.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983324_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983324-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Lambert was a key figure in keeping the group focused and getting the album completed, and typed up a script to help them understand the story and how the songs fitted together.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009220_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009220-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roger-Daltrey_in_Hamburg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Roger Daltrey singing on stage" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Roger-Daltrey_in_Hamburg.jpg/150px-Roger-Daltrey_in_Hamburg.jpg" width="150" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Roger-Daltrey_in_Hamburg.jpg/225px-Roger-Daltrey_in_Hamburg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Roger-Daltrey_in_Hamburg.jpg/300px-Roger-Daltrey_in_Hamburg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="602" data-file-height="914" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roger-Daltrey_in_Hamburg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>By the time the Who were touring <i><a href="/wiki/Tommy_(album)" title="Tommy (album)">Tommy</a></i>, Daltrey\'s stage image had changed to include long hair and open shirts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983344_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983344-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The album was released in May with the accompanying single, "Pinball Wizard", a d\xc3\xa9but performance at <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Scott%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Ronnie Scott&#39;s">Ronnie Scott\'s</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009222_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009222-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> and a tour, playing most of the new album live.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983326_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983326-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> <i>Tommy</i> sold 200,000 copies in the US in its first two weeks,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009223_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009223-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> and was a critical smash, <i><a href="/wiki/Life_(magazine)" title="Life (magazine)">Life</a></i> saying, "...&#160;for sheer power, invention and brilliance of performance, <i>Tommy</i> outstrips anything which has ever come out of a recording studio".<sup id="cite_ref-Sanctuary_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sanctuary-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Melody_Maker" title="Melody Maker">Melody Maker</a></i> declared: "Surely the Who are now the band against which all others are to be judged."<sup id="cite_ref-The_Who_Kennedy_Center_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Who_Kennedy_Center-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Daltrey had significantly improved as a singer, and set a template for rock singers in the 1970s by growing his hair long and wearing open shirts on stage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983344_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983344-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Townshend had taken to wearing a <a href="/wiki/Boiler_suit" class="mw-redirect" title="Boiler suit">boiler suit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dr._Martens" title="Dr. Martens">Doctor Martens</a> shoes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983344_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983344-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August, the Who performed at the <a href="/wiki/Woodstock_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Woodstock Festival">Woodstock Festival</a>, despite being reluctant and demanding $13,000 up front.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998240_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998240-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The group were scheduled to appear on Saturday night, 16 August,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009237_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009237-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> but the festival ran late and they did not take to the stage until 5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>am on Sunday;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvansKingsbury2009165_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvansKingsbury2009165-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> they played most of <i>Tommy</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> During their performance, <a href="/wiki/Youth_International_Party" title="Youth International Party">Yippie</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Abbie_Hoffman" title="Abbie Hoffman">Abbie Hoffman</a> interrupted the set to give a political speech about the arrest of <a href="/wiki/John_Sinclair_(poet)" title="John Sinclair (poet)">John Sinclair</a>; Townshend kicked him off stage,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998240_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998240-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> shouting: "Fuck off my fucking stage!"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009224_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009224-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvansKingsbury2009165_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvansKingsbury2009165-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> During "<a href="/wiki/See_Me,_Feel_Me" title="See Me, Feel Me">See Me, Feel Me</a>", the sun rose almost as if on cue;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998241_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998241-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Entwistle later said, "God was our lighting man".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009224_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009224-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> At the end, Townshend threw his guitar into the audience.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998241_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998241-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The set was professionally recorded and filmed, and portions appear on <a href="/wiki/Woodstock_(film)" title="Woodstock (film)">the <i>Woodstock</i> film</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Old_Grey_Whistle_Test" title="The Old Grey Whistle Test">The Old Grey Whistle Test</a></i> and <i>The Kids Are Alright</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009238_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009238-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Woodstock has been regarded as culturally significant, but the Who were critical of the event. Roadie John "Wiggie" Wolff, who arranged the band\'s payment, described it as "a shambles".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009237_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009237-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Daltrey declared it as "the worst gig &#91;they&#93; ever played"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983350_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983350-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> and Townshend said, "I thought the whole of America had gone mad."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvansKingsbury2009165_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvansKingsbury2009165-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> A more enjoyable appearance came a few weeks later at the second <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_Festival" title="Isle of Wight Festival">Isle of Wight Festival</a>, which Townshend described as "a great concert for" the band.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009240_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009240-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who_Plaque_at_University_Leeds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Plaque at Leeds University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/The_Who_Plaque_at_University_Leeds.jpg/220px-The_Who_Plaque_at_University_Leeds.jpg" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/The_Who_Plaque_at_University_Leeds.jpg/330px-The_Who_Plaque_at_University_Leeds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/The_Who_Plaque_at_University_Leeds.jpg/440px-The_Who_Plaque_at_University_Leeds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="697" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who_Plaque_at_University_Leeds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Blue_plaque" title="Blue plaque">blue plaque</a> at <a href="/wiki/Leeds_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds University">Leeds University</a>, where <i><a href="/wiki/Live_at_Leeds" title="Live at Leeds">Live at Leeds</a></i> was recorded</div></div></div>\n<p>By 1970, the Who were widely considered one of the best and most popular live rock bands; <a href="/wiki/Chris_Charlesworth" title="Chris Charlesworth">Chris Charlesworth</a> described their concerts as "leading to a kind of rock nirvana that most bands can only dream about". They decided a live album would help demonstrate how different the sound at their gigs was to <i>Tommy</i>, and set about listening to the hours of recordings they had accumulated. Townshend baulked at the prospect of doing so, and demanded that all the tapes be burned. Instead, they booked two shows, one in <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> on 14 February, and one in <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a> the following day, with the intention of recording a live album. Technical problems from the Hull gig resulted in the Leeds gig being used, which became <i><a href="/wiki/Live_at_Leeds" title="Live at Leeds">Live at Leeds</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-charlesworth_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charlesworth-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The album is viewed by several critics including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Best_Live_Album_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Best_Live_Album-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Independent_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BBCLiveatLeeds_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCLiveatLeeds-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> as one of the best live rock albums of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009426_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009426-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i>Tommy</i> tour included shows in European <a href="/wiki/Opera_house" title="Opera house">opera houses</a> and saw the Who become the first rock act to play at the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Opera" title="Metropolitan Opera">Metropolitan Opera House</a> in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983352_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983352-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In March the Who released the UK top&#160;20 hit "<a href="/wiki/The_Seeker_(The_Who_song)" title="The Seeker (The Who song)">The Seeker</a>", continuing a theme of issuing singles separate to albums. Townshend wrote the song to commemorate the common man, as a contrast to the themes on <i>Tommy</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009247,421_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009247,421-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Lifehouse_and_Who.27s_Next"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lifehouse_and_Who\'s_Next"><i>Lifehouse</i> and <i>Who\'s Next</i></span></h4>\n<p><i>Tommy</i> secured the Who\'s future, and made them millionaires. The group reacted in different ways\xe2\x80\x94Daltrey and Entwistle lived comfortably, Townshend was embarrassed at his wealth, which he felt was at odds with Meher Baba\'s ideals, and Moon spent frivolously.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983354_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983354-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the latter part of 1970, Townshend plotted a follow up <i>Tommy</i>: <i><a href="/wiki/Lifehouse_(rock_opera)" title="Lifehouse (rock opera)">Lifehouse</a></i>, which was to be a multi-media project symbolising the relationship between an artist and his audience.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983368\xe2\x80\x93369_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983368\xe2\x80\x93369-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> He developed ideas in his home studio, creating layers of synthesizers,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983373_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983373-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Young_Vic" title="Young Vic">Young Vic</a> theatre in London was booked for a series of experimental concerts. Townshend approached the gigs with optimism; the rest of the band were just happy to be gigging again.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983375_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983375-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Eventually, the others complained to Townshend that the project was too complicated and they should simply record another album. Things deteriorated until Townshend had a nervous breakdown and abandoned <i>Lifehouse</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983378_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983378-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Entwistle was the first member of the group to release a solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Smash_Your_Head_Against_the_Wall" title="Smash Your Head Against the Wall">Smash Your Head Against the Wall</a></i>, in May 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983364_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983364-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009283_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009283-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who_at_Charlotte,_NC_(1971).jpg" class="image"><img alt="The Who live in Charlotte, North Carolina, 1971" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/The_Who_at_Charlotte%2C_NC_%281971%29.jpg/220px-The_Who_at_Charlotte%2C_NC_%281971%29.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/The_Who_at_Charlotte%2C_NC_%281971%29.jpg/330px-The_Who_at_Charlotte%2C_NC_%281971%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/The_Who_at_Charlotte%2C_NC_%281971%29.jpg/440px-The_Who_at_Charlotte%2C_NC_%281971%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="434" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who_at_Charlotte,_NC_(1971).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Who at the Coliseum, Charlotte, North Carolina, 20 November 1971<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009294_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009294-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Recording at the <a href="/wiki/Record_Plant" title="Record Plant">Record Plant</a> in New York City in March 1971 was abandoned when Lambert\'s addiction to hard drugs interfered with his ability to produce.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009279,_280_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009279,_280-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The group restarted with <a href="/wiki/Glyn_Johns" title="Glyn Johns">Glyn Johns</a> in April.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009275_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009275-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>  The album was mostly <i>Lifehouse</i> material,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009279,_280_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009279,_280-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> with one unrelated song by Entwistle, "<a href="/wiki/My_Wife" title="My Wife">My Wife</a>", and was released as <i><a href="/wiki/Who%27s_Next" title="Who&#39;s Next">Who\'s Next</a></i> in August.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009288_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009288-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The album reached No.&#160;1 in the UK and No.&#160;4 in the US. "<a href="/wiki/Baba_O%27Riley" title="Baba O&#39;Riley">Baba O\'Riley</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Won%27t_Get_Fooled_Again" title="Won&#39;t Get Fooled Again">Won\'t Get Fooled Again</a>" are early examples of synthesizer use in rock, featuring keyboard sounds generated in real time by a <a href="/wiki/Lowrey_organ" title="Lowrey organ">Lowrey organ</a>; on "Won\'t Get Fooled Again", it was further processed through a <a href="/wiki/VCS3" class="mw-redirect" title="VCS3">VCS3</a> synthesizer.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009275_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009275-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The synthesizer intro to "Baba O\'Riley" was programmed based on Meher Baba\'s vital stats,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199449_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199449-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> and the track featured a violin solo by <a href="/wiki/Dave_Arbus" class="mw-redirect" title="Dave Arbus">Dave Arbus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The album was a critical and commercial success, and has been certified <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" class="mw-redirect" title="Music recording sales certification">3x platinum</a> by the <a
