href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The Who continued to issue <i>Lifehouse</i>-related material over the next few years, including the singles "<a href="/wiki/Let%27s_See_Action" title="Let&#39;s See Action">Let\'s See Action</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Join_Together_(song)" title="Join Together (song)">Join Together</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Relay_(song)" title="Relay (song)">Relay</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009421_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009421-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Whitburn_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whitburn-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The band went back on tour, and "Baba O\' Riley" and "Won\'t Get Fooled Again" became live favourites.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983392_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983392-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009277_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009277-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> In November they performed at the newly opened <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Theatre" title="Rainbow Theatre">Rainbow Theatre</a> in London for three nights,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> continuing in the US later that month, where <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hilburn" title="Robert Hilburn">Robert Hilburn</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> described the Who as "the Greatest Show on Earth".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009278_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009278-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The tour was slightly disrupted at the Civic Auditorium in San Francisco on 12 December when Moon passed out over his kit after overdosing on brandy and barbiturates.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009295_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009295-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> He recovered and completed the gig, playing to his usual strength.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998301_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998301-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Quadrophenia.2C_Tommy_film_and_The_Who_by_Numbers"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Quadrophenia,_Tommy_film_and_The_Who_by_Numbers"><i>Quadrophenia</i>, <i>Tommy</i> film and <i>The Who by Numbers</i></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who_Hamburg_1972_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The Who playing live" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/The_Who_Hamburg_1972_2.jpg/170px-The_Who_Hamburg_1972_2.jpg" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/The_Who_Hamburg_1972_2.jpg/255px-The_Who_Hamburg_1972_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/The_Who_Hamburg_1972_2.jpg/340px-The_Who_Hamburg_1972_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1260" data-file-height="1904" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who_Hamburg_1972_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Who at the Ernst-Mercke-Halle, Hamburg, 12 August 1972<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009307_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009307-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>After touring <i>Who\'s Next</i>, and needing time to write a follow-up, Townshend insisted that the Who take a lengthy break, as they had not stopped touring since the band started.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998302_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998302-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> There was no group activity until May 1972, when they started working on a proposed new album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Is_Dead%E2%80%94Long_Live_Rock!" title="Rock Is Dead\xe2\x80\x94Long Live Rock!">Rock Is Dead\xe2\x80\x94Long Live Rock!</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009302_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009302-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> but, unhappy with the recordings, abandoned the sessions. Tensions began to emerge as Townshend believed Daltrey just wanted a money-making band and Daltrey thought Townshend\'s projects were getting pretentious. Moon\'s behaviour was becoming increasingly destructive and problematic through excessive drinking and drugs use, and a desire to party and tour.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983390\xe2\x80\x9391_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983390\xe2\x80\x9391-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Daltrey performed an audit of the group\'s finances and discovered that Lambert and Stamp had not kept sufficient records. He believed them to be no longer effective managers, which Townshend and Moon disputed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983406_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983406-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The painful dissolution of the managerial and personal relationships are recounted in James D. Cooper\'s 2014 retrospective documentary, <a href="/wiki/Lambert_%26_Stamp" title="Lambert &amp; Stamp">Lambert &amp; Stamp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Following <a href="/wiki/The_Who_Tour_1972" title="The Who Tour 1972">a short European tour</a>, the remainder of 1972 was spent working on an orchestral version of <i>Tommy</i> with <a href="/wiki/Lou_Reizner" title="Lou Reizner">Lou Reizner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983401_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983401-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 1973, the Who turned to recording the album <i><a href="/wiki/Quadrophenia" title="Quadrophenia">Quadrophenia</a></i> about mod and its subculture, set against clashes with <a href="/wiki/Rockers_(youth_movement)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rockers (youth movement)">Rockers</a> in early 1960s Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983412\xe2\x80\x93413_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983412\xe2\x80\x93413-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The story is about a boy named Jimmy, who undergoes a personality crisis, and his relationship with his family, friends and mod culture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998341,344_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998341,344-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The music features four themes, reflecting the four personalities of the Who.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983420_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983420-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>  Townshend played multi-tracked synthesizers, and Entwistle played several overdubbed horn parts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983414_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983414-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> By the time the album was being recorded, relationships between the band and Lambert and Stamp had broken down irreparably, and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Curbishley" title="Bill Curbishley">Bill Curbishley</a> replaced them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983412_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983412-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The album reached No.&#160;2 in both the UK and US.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009428_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009428-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Quadrophenia tour started in <a href="/wiki/Stoke_on_Trent" class="mw-redirect" title="Stoke on Trent">Stoke on Trent</a> in October<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009335\xe2\x80\x93336_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009335\xe2\x80\x93336-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> and was immediately beset with problems. Daltrey resisted Townshend\'s wish to add <a href="/wiki/Joe_Cocker" title="Joe Cocker">Joe Cocker</a>\'s keyboardist <a href="/wiki/Chris_Stainton" title="Chris Stainton">Chris Stainton</a> (who played on the album) to the touring band.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983425\xe2\x80\x93246_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983425\xe2\x80\x93246-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> As a compromise, Townshend assembled the keyboard and synthesizer parts on backing tapes, as such a strategy had been successful with "Baba O\'Riley" and "Won\'t Get Fooled Again".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983247_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983247-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Unfortunately, the technology was not sophisticated enough to deal with the demands of the music; added to this issue, tour rehearsals had been interrupted due to an argument that culminated in Daltrey punching Townshend and knocking him out cold.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998359_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998359-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> At a gig in Newcastle, the tapes completely malfunctioned, and an enraged Townshend dragged sound-man <a href="/wiki/Bob_Pridden" title="Bob Pridden">Bob Pridden</a> on-stage, screamed at him, kicked all the amps over and partially destroyed the backing tapes. The show was abandoned for an "oldies" set, at the end of which Townshend smashed his guitar and Moon kicked over his drumkit.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009336_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009336-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998359_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998359-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Independent</i> described this gig as one of the worst of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-perrone_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perrone-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The US tour started on 20 November at the <a href="/wiki/Cow_Palace" title="Cow Palace">Cow Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Daly_City,_California" title="Daly City, California">Daly City, California</a>; Moon passed out during "Won\'t Get Fooled Again" and during "<a href="/wiki/Magic_Bus_(song)" title="Magic Bus (song)">Magic Bus</a>". Townshend asked the audience, "Can anyone play the drums?\xe2\x80\x94I mean somebody good." An audience member, <a href="/wiki/Scot_Halpin" title="Scot Halpin">Scot Halpin</a>, filled in for the rest of the show.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009337_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009337-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-perrone_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perrone-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> After a show in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, the band (except for Daltrey, who retired to bed early) caused so much damage to their hotel room, including destroying an antique painting and ramming a marble table through a wall, that <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Mounted_Police" title="Royal Canadian Mounted Police">federal law enforcement</a> arrested them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998363_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998363-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who_(1974).png" class="image"><img alt="The Who waving to a crowd" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/The_Who_%281974%29.png/220px-The_Who_%281974%29.png" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/The_Who_%281974%29.png/330px-The_Who_%281974%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/The_Who_%281974%29.png/440px-The_Who_%281974%29.png 2x" data-file-width="892" data-file-height="556" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who_(1974).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Promotional photograph celebrating the band\'s tenth anniversary, December 1974</div></div></div>\n<p>By 1974, work had begun in earnest on <a href="/wiki/Tommy_(1975_film)" title="Tommy (1975 film)">a <i>Tommy</i> film</a>. Stigwood suggested <a href="/wiki/Ken_Russell" title="Ken Russell">Ken Russell</a> as director, whose previous work Townshend had admired.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983437_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983437-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The film featured a star-studded cast, including the band members. <a href="/wiki/David_Essex" title="David Essex">David Essex</a> auditioned for the title role, but the band persuaded Daltrey to take it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983439_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983439-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The cast included <a href="/wiki/Ann-Margret" title="Ann-Margret">Ann-Margret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Reed" title="Oliver Reed">Oliver Reed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">Tina Turner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Nicholson" title="Jack Nicholson">Jack Nicholson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983439\xe2\x80\x93440_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983439\xe2\x80\x93440-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Townshend and Entwistle worked on the soundtrack for most of the year, handling the bulk of the instrumentation. Moon had moved to Los Angeles, so they used session drummers, including <a href="/wiki/Kenney_Jones" title="Kenney Jones">Kenney Jones</a>. Elton John used his own band for "Pinball Wizard".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983441_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983441-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Filming was from April<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009349\xe2\x80\x93350_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009349\xe2\x80\x93350-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> until August.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009357_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009357-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> 1500&#160;extras appeared in the "Pinball Wizard" sequence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009349\xe2\x80\x93350_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009349\xe2\x80\x93350-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The film premiered on 18 March 1975 to a standing ovation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009369_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009369-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Townshend was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Academy Award for Best Original Score">Academy Award for Best Original Score</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983451_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983451-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> <i>Tommy</i> was shown at the <a href="/wiki/1975_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="1975 Cannes Film Festival">1975 Cannes Film Festival</a>, but not in the main competition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009371\xe2\x80\x93372_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009371\xe2\x80\x93372-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> It won the award for Rock Movie of the Year in the First Annual <a href="/wiki/Rock_Music_Awards" title="Rock Music Awards">Rock Music Awards</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009373_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009373-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> and generated over $2 million in its first month.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009369_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009369-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The soundtrack reached number&#160;two on the <i>Billboard</i> charts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009430_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009430-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Keith_Moon_4_-_The_Who_-_1975.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Keith Moon behind a drumkit" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Keith_Moon_4_-_The_Who_-_1975.jpg/220px-Keith_Moon_4_-_The_Who_-_1975.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Keith_Moon_4_-_The_Who_-_1975.jpg/330px-Keith_Moon_4_-_The_Who_-_1975.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Keith_Moon_4_-_The_Who_-_1975.jpg/440px-Keith_Moon_4_-_The_Who_-_1975.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2532" data-file-height="1980" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Keith_Moon_4_-_The_Who_-_1975.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Keith_Moon" title="Keith Moon">Keith Moon</a> in 1975</div></div></div>\n<p>Work on <i>Tommy</i> took up most of 1974, and live performances by the Who were restricted to a show in May at <a href="/wiki/The_Valley_(London)" title="The Valley (London)">the Valley</a>, the home of <a href="/wiki/Charlton_Athletic_F.C." title="Charlton Athletic F.C.">Charlton Athletic</a>, in front of 80,000 fans,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009351_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009351-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> and a few dates at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> in June.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009354_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009354-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Towards the end of the year, the group released the <a href="/wiki/Out-takes" class="mw-redirect" title="Out-takes">out-takes</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/Odds_%26_Sods" title="Odds &amp; Sods">Odds &amp; Sods</a></i>, which featured several songs from the aborted <i>Lifehouse</i> project.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983446_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983446-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1975, Daltrey and Townshend disagreed about the band\'s future and criticised each other via interviews in the music paper <i><a href="/wiki/New_Musical_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="New Musical Express">New Musical Express</a></i>. Daltrey was grateful that the Who had saved him from a career as a sheet-metal worker and was unhappy at Townshend not playing well; Townshend felt the commitment of the group prevented him from releasing solo material.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983458_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983458-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The next album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Who_by_Numbers" title="The Who by Numbers">The Who by Numbers</a></i>, had introspective songs from Townshend that dealt with disillusionment such as "However Much I Booze" and "How Many Friends"; they resembled his later solo work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983460_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983460-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Entwistle\'s "Success Story" gave a humorous look at the music industry, and "<a href="/wiki/Squeeze_Box_(The_Who_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Squeeze Box (The Who song)">Squeeze Box</a>" was a hit single.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009364_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009364-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> The group toured from October, playing little new material and few <i>Quadrophenia</i> numbers, and reintroducing several from <i>Tommy</i>. The American leg of the tour began in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> to a crowd of 18,000 at <a href="/wiki/The_Summit_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="The Summit Arena">The Summit Arena</a>, and was supported by <a href="/wiki/Toots_and_the_Maytals" title="Toots and the Maytals">Toots and the Maytals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009365_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009365-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> On 6 December 1975, the Who set the record for largest indoor concert at the <a href="/wiki/Pontiac_Silverdome" title="Pontiac Silverdome">Pontiac Silverdome</a>, attended by 78,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998443_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998443-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> On 31 May 1976, they played a second concert at the Valley which was listed in the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness Book of Records</a></i> as the world\'s loudest concert at over 120&#160;dB.<sup id="cite_ref-Sanctuary_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sanctuary-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Townshend had become fed up of touring<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983473_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983473-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> but Entwistle considered live performance to be at a peak.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998465_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998465-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Who_Are_You_and_Moon.27s_death"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Who_Are_You_and_Moon\'s_death"><i>Who Are You</i> and Moon\'s death</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Daltrey_and_Townshend.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Roger Daltrey singing and Pete Townshend singing and playing a guitar" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Daltrey_and_Townshend.jpg/220px-Daltrey_and_Townshend.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Daltrey_and_Townshend.jpg/330px-Daltrey_and_Townshend.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Daltrey_and_Townshend.jpg/440px-Daltrey_and_Townshend.jpg 2x" data-file-width="509" data-file-height="349" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Daltrey_and_Townshend.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Daltrey and Townshend, 21 October 1976, Maple Leaf Gardens, Toronto, Ontario\xe2\x80\x94their last ever public gig with Moon</div></div></div>\n<p>After the 1976 tour, Townshend took most of the following year off to spend time with his family.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009394_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009394-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> He discovered that former Beatles and Rolling Stones manager <a href="/wiki/Allen_Klein" title="Allen Klein">Allen Klein</a> had bought a stake in his publishing company. A settlement was reached, but Townshend was upset and disillusioned that Klein had attempted to take ownership of his songs. Townshend went to the <a href="/wiki/Speakeasy_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Speakeasy Club">Speakeasy</a> where he met <a href="/wiki/The_Sex_Pistols" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sex Pistols">the Sex Pistols</a>\' Steve Jones and Paul Cook, fans of the Who. After leaving, he passed out in a doorway, where a policeman said he would not be arrested if he could stand and walk. The events inspired the title track of the next album, <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Are_You" title="Who Are You">Who Are You</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009396_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009396-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The group reconvened in September 1977, but Townshend announced there would be no live performances for the immediate future, a decision that Daltrey endorsed. By this point, Moon was so unhealthy that the Who conceded it would be difficult for him to cope with touring. The only gig that year was an informal show on 15 December at the <a href="/wiki/Gaumont_State_Cinema" title="Gaumont State Cinema">Gaumont State Cinema</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kilburn,_London" title="Kilburn, London">Kilburn</a>, London, filmed for the documentary, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Kids_Are_Alright_(film)" title="The Kids Are Alright (film)">The Kids Are Alright</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009406_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009406-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> The band had not played for 14 months, and their performance was so weak that the footage was unused. Moon\'s playing was particularly lacklustre and he had gained a lot of weight,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983494_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983494-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> though Daltrey later said, "even at his worst, Keith Moon was amazing."<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Recording of <i>Who Are You</i> started in January 1978. Daltrey clashed with Johns over the production of his vocals, and Moon\'s drumming was so poor that Daltrey and Entwistle considered firing him. Moon\'s playing improved, but on one track, "Music Must Change", he was replaced as he could not play in 6/8 time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983496_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983496-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> In May, the Who filmed another performance at Shepperton Sound Studios for <i>The Kids Are Alright</i>. This performance was strong, and several tracks were used in the film. It was the last gig Moon performed with the Who.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983499_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983499-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The album was released on 18 August, and became their biggest and fastest seller to date, peaking at No.&#160;6 in the UK and No.&#160;2 in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009430_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009430-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Instead of touring, Daltrey, Townshend and Moon did a series of promotional television interviews, and Entwistle worked on the soundtrack for <i>The Kids Are Alright</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983504\xe2\x80\x93505_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983504\xe2\x80\x93505-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 September, Moon attended a party held by <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a> to celebrate <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Holly" title="Buddy Holly">Buddy Holly</a>\'s birthday. Returning to his flat, Moon took 32 tablets of <a href="/wiki/Clomethiazole" title="Clomethiazole">clomethiazole</a> which had been prescribed to combat his <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_withdrawal" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcohol withdrawal">alcohol withdrawal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009416_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009416-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> He passed out the following morning and was discovered dead later that day.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983506\xe2\x80\x93507_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983506\xe2\x80\x93507-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009416_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009416-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1978.E2.80.931983"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1978\xe2\x80\x931983">1978\xe2\x80\x931983</span></h3>\n<p>The day after Moon\'s death, Townshend issued the statement: "We are more determined than ever to carry on, and we want the spirit of the group to which Keith contributed so much to go on, although no human being can ever take his place."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009416\xe2\x80\x93417_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009416\xe2\x80\x93417-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Drummer <a href="/wiki/Phil_Collins" title="Phil Collins">Phil Collins</a>, having a temporary break from <a href="/wiki/Genesis_(band)" title="Genesis (band)">Genesis</a> after his first marriage had failed, was at a loose end and asked to replace Moon, but Townshend had already asked Jones, who had previously played with the Small Faces and the Faces. Jones officially joined the band in November 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETownshend2012287_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETownshend2012287-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Bundrick" title="John Bundrick">John "Rabbit" Bundrick</a> joined the live band as an unofficial keyboardist.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETownshend2012289_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETownshend2012289-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> On 2 May 1979, the Who returned to the stage with a concert at the Rainbow Theatre, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a> in France<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983509_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983509-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> and dates at Madison Square Garden in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983510_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983510-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Quadrophenia_(film)" title="Quadrophenia (film)">The <i>Quadrophenia</i> film</a> was released that year. It was directed by <a href="/wiki/Franc_Roddam" title="Franc Roddam">Franc Roddam</a> in his feature-directing d\xc3\xa9but,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998518_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998518-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> and had straightforward acting rather than musical numbers as in <i>Tommy</i>. <a href="/wiki/John_Lydon" title="John Lydon">John Lydon</a> was considered for Jimmy, but the role went to <a href="/wiki/Phil_Daniels" title="Phil Daniels">Phil Daniels</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a> played Jimmy\'s friend and fellow mod, the Ace Face.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The soundtrack was Jones\' first appearance on a Who record, performing on newly written material not on the original album.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> The film was a critical and box office success in the UK<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998535_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998535-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> and appealed to the growing <a href="/wiki/Mod_revival" title="Mod revival">mod revival</a> movement. <a href="/wiki/The_Jam" title="The Jam">The Jam</a> were influenced by the Who, and critics noticed a similarity between Townshend and the group\'s leader, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Weller" title="Paul Weller">Paul Weller</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983510_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983510-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>The Kids Are Alright</i> was also completed in 1979. It was a retrospective of the band\'s career, directed by Jeff Stein.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983486_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983486-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> The film included footage of the band at Monterey, Woodstock and Pontiac, and clips from the Smothers Brothers\' show and <i><a href="/wiki/Russell_Harty" title="Russell Harty">Russell Harty Plus</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998486_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998486-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Moon had died one week after seeing the rough cut with Daltrey. The film contains the Shepperton concert,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998503_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998503-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> and an audio track of him playing over silent footage of himself was the last time he ever played the drums.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998514_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998514-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December, the Who became the third band, after the Beatles and <a href="/wiki/The_Band" title="The Band">the Band</a>, to appear on the cover of <i>Time</i>. The article, by <a href="/wiki/Jay_Cocks" title="Jay Cocks">Jay Cocks</a>, said the band had outpaced, outlasted, outlived and outclassed all of their rock band contemporaries.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_Magazine_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time_Magazine-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cincinnati_tragedy">Cincinnati tragedy</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Who_concert_disaster" title="The Who concert disaster">The Who concert disaster</a></div>\n<p>On 3 December 1979, a crowd crush at a Who gig at the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Arena" title="U.S. Bank Arena">Riverfront Coliseum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati" title="Cincinnati">Cincinnati</a> killed 11 fans.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> This was partly due to the <a href="/wiki/Festival_seating" class="mw-redirect" title="Festival seating">festival seating</a>, where the first to enter get the best positions. Some fans waiting outside mistook the band\'s <a href="/wiki/Soundcheck" title="Soundcheck">soundcheck</a> for the concert, and attempted to force their way inside. As only a few entrance doors were opened, a bottleneck situation ensued with thousands trying to gain entry, and the crush became deadly.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983512_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983512-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Who were not told until after the show because civic authorities feared crowd problems if the concert were cancelled. The band were deeply shaken upon learning of it and requested that appropriate safety precautions be taken in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983513_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983513-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> The following evening, in <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo, New York</a>, Daltrey told the crowd that the band had "lost a lot of family last night and this show\'s for them".<sup id="cite_ref-stampede_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stampede-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Change_and_break-up">Change and break-up</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BouncingTownshend.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Roger Daltrey holding a microphone and Pete Townshend jumping on stage" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/BouncingTownshend.jpg/220px-BouncingTownshend.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/BouncingTownshend.jpg/330px-BouncingTownshend.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/BouncingTownshend.jpg/440px-BouncingTownshend.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1594" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BouncingTownshend.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Who in Toronto, 1980</div></div></div>\n<p>Daltrey took a break in 1980 to work on the film <i><a href="/wiki/McVicar_(film)" title="McVicar (film)">McVicar</a></i>, in which he took the lead role of bank robber <a href="/wiki/John_McVicar" title="John McVicar">John McVicar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983492_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983492-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/McVicar_(album)" title="McVicar (album)">soundtrack album</a> is a Daltrey solo album, though all members of the Who are included in the supporting musicians, and was his most successful solo release.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Who released two studio albums with Jones as drummer, <i><a href="/wiki/Face_Dances" title="Face Dances">Face Dances</a></i> (1981) and <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Hard" title="It&#39;s Hard">It\'s Hard</a></i> (1982). <i>Face Dances</i> produced a US top&#160;20 and UK top ten hit with the single "<a href="/wiki/You_Better_You_Bet" title="You Better You Bet">You Better You Bet</a>", whose video was one of the first shown on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Both <i>Face Dances</i> and <i>It\'s Hard</i> sold well and the latter received a five-star review in <i>Rolling Stone</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> The single "<a href="/wiki/Eminence_Front" title="Eminence Front">Eminence Front</a>" from <i>It\'s Hard</i> was a hit, and became a regular at live shows.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By this time Townshend had fallen into depression, wondering if he was no longer a visionary.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983514_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983514-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> He was again at odds with Daltrey and Entwistle, who merely wanted to tour and play hits<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983517\xe2\x80\x93518_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983517\xe2\x80\x93518-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> and thought Townshend had saved his best songs for his solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Empty_Glass" title="Empty Glass">Empty Glass</a></i> (1980).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983519_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983519-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Jones\' drumming style was very different from Moon\'s and this drew criticism within the band.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983517\xe2\x80\x93518_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983517\xe2\x80\x93518-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Townshend briefly became addicted to heroin before cleaning up early in 1982 after treatment with <a href="/wiki/Meg_Patterson" title="Meg Patterson">Meg Patterson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983523_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983523-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Entwisle_1987.jpg" class="image"><img alt="John Entwistle playing a bass guitar" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/John_Entwisle_1987.jpg/220px-John_Entwisle_1987.jpg" width="220" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/John_Entwisle_1987.jpg/330px-John_Entwisle_1987.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/John_Entwisle_1987.jpg/440px-John_Entwisle_1987.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1406" data-file-height="1172" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Entwisle_1987.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>John Entwistle performing with the Who at the Manchester Apollo, 1981</div></div></div>\n<p>Townshend wanted the Who to stop touring and become a studio act; Entwistle threatened to quit, saying, "I don\'t intend to get off the road&#160;... there\'s not much I can do about it except hope they change their minds."<sup id="cite_ref-greene82_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greene82-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Townshend did not change his mind, and so the Who embarked on a farewell tour of the US and Canada<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/The_Clash" title="The Clash">the Clash</a> as support,<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> ending in Toronto on 17 December 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-greene82_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greene82-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Townshend spent part of 1983 writing material for a Who studio album owed to <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a> from a contract in 1980,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983524_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983524-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> but he found himself unable to generate music appropriate for the Who and at the end of 1983 paid for himself and Jones to be released from the contract.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998538_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998538-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> On 16 December 1983, Townshend announced at a press conference that he was leaving the Who, effectively ending the band.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the Who break-up, Townshend focused on solo albums such as <i><a href="/wiki/White_City:_A_Novel" title="White City: A Novel">White City: A Novel</a></i> (1985), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Iron_Man:_A_Musical" class="mw-redirect" title="The Iron Man: A Musical">The Iron Man</a></i> (1989, featuring Daltrey and Entwistle and two songs credited to the Who), and <i><a href="/wiki/Psychoderelict" title="Psychoderelict">Psychoderelict</a></i> (1993).<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reunions">Reunions</span></h3>\n<p>In July 1985, the Who performed at <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>, London.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> The BBC transmission truck blew a fuse during the set, temporarily interrupting the broadcast.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/List_of_BRIT_Awards_ceremonies#1988" class="mw-redirect" title="List of BRIT Awards ceremonies">1988</a> <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>, the band was given the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a>\'s Lifetime Achievement Award.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> The short set they played there was the last time Jones played with the Who.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1989_tour">1989 tour</span></h4>\n<p>In 1989, the band embarked on a 25th-anniversary <i>The Kids Are Alright</i> reunion tour with <a href="/wiki/Simon_Phillips_(drummer)" title="Simon Phillips (drummer)">Simon Phillips</a> on drums and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Bolton" title="Steve Bolton">Steve "Boltz" Bolton</a> as a second guitarist. Townshend had announced in 1987 that he suffered from <a href="/wiki/Tinnitus" title="Tinnitus">tinnitus</a><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> and alternated acoustic, rhythm, and lead guitar to preserve his hearing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998539_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998539-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Their two shows at Sullivan Stadium in <a href="/wiki/Foxborough,_Massachusetts" title="Foxborough, Massachusetts">Foxborough, Massachusetts</a>, sold 100,000 tickets in less than eight hours, beating previous records set there by <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> The tour was briefly marred at a gig in Tacoma, Washington, where Townshend injured his arm on-stage.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Some critics disliked the tour\'s over-produced and expanded line-up, calling it "The Who on Ice";<sup id="cite_ref-greene_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greene-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> at <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> said the tour "tarnished the reputation of the Who almost irreparably".<sup id="cite_ref-jointogether_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jointogether-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> The tour included most of <i>Tommy</i> and included such guests as <a href="/wiki/Phil_Collins" title="Phil Collins">Phil Collins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Idol" title="Billy Idol">Billy Idol</a> and Elton John.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> A 2-CD live album, <i><a href="/wiki/Join_Together_(album)" title="Join Together (album)">Join Together</a></i>, was released in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-jointogether_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jointogether-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Partial_reunions">Partial reunions</span></h4>\n<p>In 1990, the Who were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998540_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998540-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> The group have a featured collection in the hall\'s museum, including one of Moon\'s velvet suits, a <a href="/wiki/Warwick_(company)" title="Warwick (company)">Warwick</a> bass of Entwistle\'s, and a <a href="/wiki/Drumhead" title="Drumhead">drumhead</a> from 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1991, the Who recorded a cover of Elton John\'s "<a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night%27s_Alright_for_Fighting" title="Saturday Night&#39;s Alright for Fighting">Saturday Night\'s Alright for Fighting</a>" for the tribute album <i><a href="/wiki/Two_Rooms:_Celebrating_the_Songs_of_Elton_John_%26_Bernie_Taupin" title="Two Rooms: Celebrating the Songs of Elton John &amp; Bernie Taupin">Two Rooms: Celebrating the Songs of Elton John &amp; Bernie Taupin</a></i>. It was the last studio recording to feature Entwistle. In 1994, Daltrey turned 50 and celebrated with two concerts at New York\'s <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Hall" title="Carnegie Hall">Carnegie Hall</a>. The shows included guest spots by Entwistle and Townshend. Although all three surviving original members of the Who attended, they appeared on stage together only during the finale, "Join Together", with the other guests. Daltrey toured that year with Entwistle, <a href="/wiki/Zak_Starkey" title="Zak Starkey">Zak Starkey</a> on drums and <a href="/wiki/Simon_Townshend" title="Simon Townshend">Simon Townshend</a> filling in for his brother as guitarist.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998542_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998542-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Re-formation">Re-formation</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Revival_of_Quadrophenia">Revival of <i>Quadrophenia</i></span></h4>\n<p>In 1996, Townshend, Entwistle and Daltrey performed <i>Quadrophenia</i> with guests and Starkey on drums at <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998543_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998543-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> The performance was narrated by Daniels, who had played Jimmy in the 1979 film. Despite technical difficulties the show led to a six-night residency at Madison Square Garden and a <a href="/wiki/The_Who_Tour_1996%E2%80%931997" title="The Who Tour 1996\xe2\x80\x931997">US and European tour through 1996 and 1997</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998543_255-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998543-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Townshend played mostly acoustic guitar, but eventually was persuaded to play some electric.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> In 1998, <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> ranked the Who ninth in their list of the "100 Greatest Artists of Rock \'n\' Roll".<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Charity_shows_and_Entwistle.27s_death"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_shows_and_Entwistle\'s_death">Charity shows and Entwistle\'s death</span></h4>\n<p>In late 1999, the Who performed as a five-piece for the first time since 1985, with Bundrick on keyboards and Starkey on drums. The first show in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> at the <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Garden_Arena" title="MGM Grand Garden Arena">MGM Grand Garden Arena</a><sup id="cite_ref-greene_249-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greene-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> was partially broadcast on TV and the Internet and released as the DVD <i><a href="/wiki/The_Vegas_Job" title="The Vegas Job">The Vegas Job</a></i>. They then performed acoustic shows at <a href="/wiki/Neil_Young" title="Neil Young">Neil Young</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Bridge_School_Benefit" title="Bridge School Benefit">Bridge School Benefit</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Shoreline_Amphitheatre" title="Shoreline Amphitheatre">Shoreline Amphitheatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">Mountain View, California</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> followed by gigs at the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Blues" title="House of Blues">House of Blues</a> in Chicago<sup id="cite_ref-official_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-official-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> and two Christmas charity shows at the <a href="/wiki/Shepherds_Bush_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Shepherds Bush Empire">Shepherds Bush Empire</a> in London.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> Critics were delighted to see a rejuvenated band with a basic line-up comparable to the tours of the 1960s and 1970s. Andy Greene in <i>Rolling Stone</i> called the 1999 tour better than the final one with Moon in 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-greene_249-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greene-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The band toured the US and UK from June to October 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-official_259-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-official-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> to generally favourable reviews,<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> culminating in a charity show at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> for the Teenage Cancer trust with guest performances from <a href="/wiki/Paul_Weller" title="Paul Weller">Paul Weller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Vedder" title="Eddie Vedder">Eddie Vedder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noel_Gallagher" title="Noel Gallagher">Noel Gallagher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Adams" title="Bryan Adams">Bryan Adams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Kennedy" title="Nigel Kennedy">Nigel Kennedy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> Stephen Tomas Erlewine described the gig as "an exceptional reunion concert".<sup id="cite_ref-alberthall_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alberthall-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> In 2001 the band performed <a href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_New_York_City" title="The Concert for New York City">the Concert for New York City</a> at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> for families of firefighters and police who had lost their lives following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> on the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973%E2%80%932001)" title="World Trade Center (1973\xe2\x80\x932001)">World Trade Center</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-usatoday200110_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday200110-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> and were honoured with a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lifetime_Grammy_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lifetime_Grammy-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Who played concerts in the UK in early 2002 in preparation for a full US tour. On 27 June, the day before the first date,<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> Entwistle was found dead of a heart attack at 57 at the <a href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Hotel_and_Casino_(Las_Vegas)" title="Hard Rock Hotel and Casino (Las Vegas)">Hard Rock Hotel</a> in Las Vegas. <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">Cocaine</a> was a contributing factor.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="After_Entwistle:_Tours_and_Endless_Wire">After Entwistle: Tours and <i>Endless Wire</i></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who_2007_-2-.JPG" class="image"><img alt="On-stage shot of the Who" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/The_Who_2007_-2-.JPG/220px-The_Who_2007_-2-.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/The_Who_2007_-2-.JPG/330px-The_Who_2007_-2-.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/The_Who_2007_-2-.JPG/440px-The_Who_2007_-2-.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1516" data-file-height="852" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who_2007_-2-.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Who on Tour in 2007. L to R: <a href="/wiki/Zak_Starkey" title="Zak Starkey">Zak Starkey</a>, Daltrey, Townshend, and <a href="/wiki/John_%22Rabbit%22_Bundrick" class="mw-redirect" title="John &quot;Rabbit&quot; Bundrick">John "Rabbit" Bundrick</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Entwistle\'s son, Christopher, gave a statement supporting the Who\'s decision to carry on. The US tour began at the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Bowl" title="Hollywood Bowl">Hollywood Bowl</a> with touring bassist <a href="/wiki/Pino_Palladino" title="Pino Palladino">Pino Palladino</a>. Townshend dedicated the show to Entwistle, and ended with a montage of pictures of him. The tour lasted until September.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> The loss of a founding member of the Who caused Townshend to re-evaluate his relationship with Daltrey, which had been strained over the band\'s career. He decided their friendship was important, and this ultimately led to writing and recording new material.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt20061029_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20061029-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To combat <a href="/wiki/Bootleg_recording" title="Bootleg recording">bootlegging</a>, the band began to release the <a href="/wiki/Encore_Series_2002" class="mw-redirect" title="Encore Series 2002">Encore Series</a> of official <a href="/wiki/Soundboard_recording" title="Soundboard recording">soundboard recordings</a> via themusic.com. An official statement read: "to satisfy this demand they have agreed to release their own official recordings to benefit worthy causes".<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2004, the Who released "Old Red Wine" and "Real Good Looking Boy" (with Palladino and <a href="/wiki/Greg_Lake" title="Greg Lake">Greg Lake</a>, respectively, on bass) on a singles anthology, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Who:_Then_and_Now" class="mw-redirect" title="The Who: Then and Now">The Who: Then and Now</a></i>, and went on an <a href="/wiki/The_Who_Tour_2004" title="The Who Tour 2004">18-date tour</a> of Japan, Australia, the UK and the US, including a return appearance at the Isle of Wight.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, <i>Rolling Stone</i> ranked the Who No.&#160;29 on their list of the <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_100_Greatest_Artists_of_All_Time" title="Rolling Stone&#39;s 100 Greatest Artists of All Time">100 Greatest Artists of All Time</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zak_Starkey2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Zak Starkey playing drums" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Zak_Starkey2.jpg/220px-Zak_Starkey2.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Zak_Starkey2.jpg/330px-Zak_Starkey2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Zak_Starkey2.jpg/440px-Zak_Starkey2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zak_Starkey2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Zak Starkey has been the Who\'s main drummer since 1994, and turned down an invitation to be a full-time member.<sup id="cite_ref-townshend200612_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-townshend200612-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The Who announced in 2005 that they were working on a new album. Townshend posted a novella called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boy_Who_Heard_Music" title="The Boy Who Heard Music">The Boy Who Heard Music</a></i> on his blog, which developed into a mini-opera called <i><a href="/wiki/Wire_%26_Glass" title="Wire &amp; Glass">Wire&#160;&amp; Glass</a></i>, forming the basis for the album.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt20061029_269-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20061029-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Endless_Wire_(The_Who_album)" title="Endless Wire (The Who album)">Endless Wire</a></i>, released in 2006, was the first full studio album of new material since 1982\'s <i>It\'s Hard</i> and contained the band\'s first mini-opera since "Rael" in 1967. The album reached No.&#160;7 in the US and No.&#160;9 in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> Starkey was invited to join Oasis in April 2006 and the Who in November 2006, but he declined and split his time between the two.<sup id="cite_ref-townshend200612_273-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-townshend200612-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2007, the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Amazing_Journey:_The_Story_of_the_Who" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazing Journey: The Story of the Who">Amazing Journey: The Story of the Who</a></i> was released, featuring unreleased footage of the 1970 Leeds appearance and a 1964 performance at the Railway Hotel when the group were The High Numbers. <i>Amazing Journey</i> was nominated for a 2009 Grammy Award.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Super_Bowl_44_South_Florida_Halftime_Show_the_Who_(4344082917)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Super_Bowl_44_South_Florida_Halftime_Show_the_Who_%284344082917%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Super_Bowl_44_South_Florida_Halftime_Show_the_Who_%284344082917%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Super_Bowl_44_South_Florida_Halftime_Show_the_Who_%284344082917%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Super_Bowl_44_South_Florida_Halftime_Show_the_Who_%284344082917%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Super_Bowl_44_South_Florida_Halftime_Show_the_Who_%284344082917%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Super_Bowl_44_South_Florida_Halftime_Show_the_Who_%284344082917%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1383" data-file-height="983" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Super_Bowl_44_South_Florida_Halftime_Show_the_Who_(4344082917)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Who performing the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLIV" title="Super Bowl XLIV">2010</a> <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Super_Bowl_halftime_shows" title="List of Super Bowl halftime shows">halftime show</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Who toured in support of <i>Endless Wire</i>, including the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2_Electric_Proms" title="BBC Radio 2 Electric Proms">BBC Electric Proms</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Roundhouse_(venue)" title="Roundhouse (venue)">Roundhouse</a> in London in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> headlining the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> a half-time appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLIV" title="Super Bowl XLIV">Super Bowl XLIV</a> in 2010<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> and being the final act at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_closing_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics closing ceremony">closing ceremony</a> of the London <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Olympic Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-olympics_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olympics-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup>  In November 2012, the Who released <i><a href="/wiki/Live_at_Hull" class="mw-redirect" title="Live at Hull">Live at Hull</a></i>, an album of the band\'s performance night after the <i>Live at Leeds</i> gig.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Quadrophenia_and_More">Quadrophenia and More</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Quadrophenia_and_More" class="mw-redirect" title="Quadrophenia and More">Quadrophenia and More</a></div>\n<p>In 2010, the Who performed <i>Quadrophenia</i> with parts played by Vedder and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Meighan" title="Tom Meighan">Tom Meighan</a> at the Royal Albert Hall as part of the <a href="/wiki/Teenage_Cancer_Trust" title="Teenage Cancer Trust">Teenage Cancer Trust</a> series of 10 gigs.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> A planned tour for early 2010 was jeopardised by the return of Townshend\'s tinnitus. He experimented with an in-ear monitoring system that was recommended by <a href="/wiki/Neil_Young" title="Neil Young">Neil Young</a> and his audiologist.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Quadrophenia_and_More" class="mw-redirect" title="Quadrophenia and More">Quadrophenia and More</a></i> tour started in November 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a><sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> with keyboardists John Corey, <a href="/wiki/Loren_Gold" title="Loren Gold">Loren Gold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Simes" title="Frank Simes">Frank Simes</a>, the latter of whom was also musical director.<sup id="cite_ref-thewho20120718_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thewho20120718-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> In February 2013, Starkey pulled a tendon and was replaced for a gig by <a href="/wiki/Scott_Devours" title="Scott Devours">Scott Devours</a> who performed with less than four hours\' notice.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> The tour moved to Europe and the UK, and ended at the <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Arena" title="Wembley Arena">Wembley Arena</a> in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="The_Who_Hits_50.21_and_beyond"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Who_Hits_50!_and_beyond"><i>The Who Hits 50!</i> and beyond</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who,_Oakland,_CA,_May_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/The_Who%2C_Oakland%2C_CA%2C_May_2016.jpg/220px-The_Who%2C_Oakland%2C_CA%2C_May_2016.jpg" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/The_Who%2C_Oakland%2C_CA%2C_May_2016.jpg/330px-The_Who%2C_Oakland%2C_CA%2C_May_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/The_Who%2C_Oakland%2C_CA%2C_May_2016.jpg/440px-The_Who%2C_Oakland%2C_CA%2C_May_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2424" data-file-height="2286" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Who,_Oakland,_CA,_May_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Daltrey and Townshend on the <i>Who Hits 50!</i> tour in 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>In October 2013, Townshend announced the Who would stage their final tour in 2015, performing in locations they have never played before.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Daltrey clarified that the tour is unrelated to the band\'s 50th anniversary\xe2\x80\x94which occurred in 2013\xe2\x80\x94and indicated that he and Townshend were considering recording new material but would be emphasising their hits in their final stadium tour.<sup id="cite_ref-rsm2015_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsm2015-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> Daltrey stated, "We can\'t go on touring forever&#160;... it could be open-ended, but it will have a finality to it."<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2014, Jones reunited with the Who at a charity gig for Prostate Cancer UK his Hurtwood Polo Club, alongside <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Procol_Harum" title="Procol Harum">Procol Harum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Rutherford" title="Mike Rutherford">Mike Rutherford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gs_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gs-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, the Who announced plans for a world tour with a possible accompanying album.<sup id="cite_ref-rs2015_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs2015-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> In September, the Who released the song "<a href="/wiki/Be_Lucky" title="Be Lucky">Be Lucky</a>", which was included on the compilation <i><a href="/wiki/The_Who_Hits_50!_(album)" title="The Who Hits 50! (album)">The Who Hits 50!</a></i> in October.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> That November, the group released a virtual reality app co-designed by Daltrey\'s son, Jamie, featuring events and images from the band\'s history.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2015, the Who headlined that year\'s <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park</a> Festival, and two days later, the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival</a>. Townshend suggested to <i><a href="/wiki/Mojo_(magazine)" title="Mojo (magazine)">Mojo</a></i> that it could be the group\'s last UK gig.<sup id="cite_ref-mojo2015_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojo2015-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> To coincide with The Who\'s 50th anniversary, all studio albums, including the new compilation, <i>The Who Hits 50!</i>, were reissued on vinyl.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> In September 2015, all remaining US tour dates were cancelled after Daltrey contracted <a href="/wiki/Viral_meningitis" title="Viral meningitis">viral meningitis</a>. Then Townshend promised the band would come back "stronger than ever".<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 June 2016 in <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Isle_of_Wight" title="Newport, Isle of Wight">Newport</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, The Who embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Who_Tour_51!" title="Back to the Who Tour 51!">Back to the Who Tour 51!</a>, a new tour seen as a continuation of the previous year\'s tour.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> The new tour included a return visit to the Isle of Wight Festival (at the Seaclose Park in Newport, England) on the opening date on 11 June 2016 and ended at the Empire Polo Grounds in <a href="/wiki/Indio,_CA" class="mw-redirect" title="Indio, CA">Indio, CA</a> on 16 October 2016 after thirteen concerts.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-axs.com_The_Who_Tommy_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-axs.com_The_Who_Tommy-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thewho.com_Tommy_2017_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thewho.com_Tommy_2017-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> In November 2016, The Who announced that 5 UK dates the following April (previously scheduled for that August and September), would include a full live performance of <i>Tommy</i>. The 5-date tour was renamed "<a href="/wiki/2017_Tommy_%26_More" title="2017 Tommy &amp; More">2017 Tommy &amp; More</a>", and was the first time that the band played <i>Tommy</i> in full since 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-teamrock.com_2017_Tommy_&amp;_More_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamrock.com_2017_Tommy_&amp;_More-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style_and_equipment">Musical style and equipment</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Who%27s_musical_equipment" title="The Who&#39;s musical equipment">The Who\'s musical equipment</a></div>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25em;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9c ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"The music of the Who can only be called rock &amp; roll&#160;... it is neither derivative of folk music nor the blues; the primary influence is rock &amp; roll itself."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94 <a href="/wiki/Jann_Wenner" title="Jann Wenner">Jann Wenner</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198389_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198389-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>The Who have been regarded primarily as a rock band, yet have taken influence from several other styles of music during their career. The original group played a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Trad_jazz" title="Trad jazz">trad jazz</a> and contemporary pop hits as the Detours, and R&amp;B in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200922,_26_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200922,_26-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> The group move to a mod sound the following year, particularly after hearing the Small Faces fuse Motown with a harsher R&amp;B sound.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200938\xe2\x80\x9339_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200938\xe2\x80\x9339-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> The group\'s early work was geared towards singles, though it was not straightforward pop. In 1967, Townshend coined the term "<a href="/wiki/Power_pop" title="Power pop">power pop</a>" to describe the Who\'s style.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983253_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983253-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> Like their contemporaries, the group were influenced by the arrival of Hendrix, particularly after the Who and the Experience met at Monterey.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998189_77-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998189-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> This and lengthy touring strengthened the band\'s sound. In the studio, they began to develop softer pieces, particularly from <i>Tommy</i> onwards,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998232_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998232-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> and turned their attention towards albums more than singles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECampbell2012239_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECampbell2012239-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">\n<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Won%27t_Get_Fooled_Again.ogg" title="File:Won&#39;t Get Fooled Again.ogg">Brief sample from the song "Won\'t Get Fooled Again"</a></div>\n<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_1" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="30.185941043084" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Won&#39;t_Get_Fooled_Again.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b6/Won%27t_Get_Fooled_Again.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (97 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="96599" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/b/b6/Won%27t_Get_Fooled_Again.ogg/Won%27t_Get_Fooled_Again.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="212744" /></audio></div></div>\n<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">The closing section of "Won\'t Get Fooled Again" merges Townshend\'s synthesised organ with power chords, Moon\'s drum fills and "the greatest scream of a career".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983388_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983388-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup></div></div></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>From the early 1970s, the band\'s sound included synthesizers, particularly on <i>Who\'s Next</i> and <i>Quadrophenia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAtkins2000177_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAtkins2000177-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> Although groups had used synthesizers before, the Who were one of the first to integrate the sound into a basic rock structure.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAtkins2000140_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAtkins2000140-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> In <i>By Numbers</i> the group\'s style had scaled back to more standard rock,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAtkins2000222_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAtkins2000222-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> but synthesisers regained prominence on <i>Face Dances</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Townshend and Entwistle were instrumental in making extreme volumes and <a href="/wiki/Distortion_(music)" title="Distortion (music)">distortion</a> standard rock practices.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAtkins200014,_16_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAtkins200014,_16-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup>  The Who were early adopters of <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Amplification" title="Marshall Amplification">Marshall Amplification</a>. Entwistle was the first member to get two 4\xc3\x9712 <a href="/wiki/Instrument_amplifier#Standard_amp" title="Instrument amplifier">speaker cabinets</a>, quickly followed by Townshend.
