The group used <a href="/wiki/Audio_feedback" title="Audio feedback">feedback</a> as part of their guitar sound, both live and in the studio.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200943_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200943-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarison2014199_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarison2014199-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> In 1967, Townshend changed to using Sound City amplifiers, customised by Dave Reeves, then in 1970 to <a href="/wiki/Hiwatt" title="Hiwatt">Hiwatt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-drozdowski_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drozdowski-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> The group were the first to use a 1000&#160;watt <a href="/wiki/Public_address_system" title="Public address system">PA systems</a> for live gigs, which led to competition from bands such as the Rolling Stones and <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Throughout their careers, the members of the Who have said their live sound has never been captured as they wished on record.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent20092_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent20092-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> Live gigs and the audience have always been important to the group. "Irish" Jack Lyons said, "The Who weren\'t a joke, they were fucking real, and so were we."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh19839_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh19839-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocals">Vocals</span></h3>\n<p>Daltrey initially based his style on Motown and rock and roll,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198343_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198343-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup> but from <i>Tommy</i> onwards he tackled a wider range of styles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983328_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983328-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> His trademark sound with the band, as noted in 1983, has been a characteristic scream, as heard at the end of "Won\'t Get Fooled Again".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983388,496_327-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983388,496-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Group backing vocals are prominent in the Who. After "I Can\'t Explain" used session men for backing vocals, Townshend and Entwistle resolved to do better themselves on subsequent releases, producing strong backing harmonies.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> Daltrey, Townshend and Entwistle sang lead on various songs, and occasionally Moon joined in. <i>Who\'s Next</i> featured Daltrey and Townshend sharing the lead vocals on several songs, and biographer Dave Marsh considers the contrast between Daltrey\'s strong, guttural baritone and Townshend\'s higher and gentler tenor to be one of the album\'s highlights.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983386_329-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983386-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Daltrey\'s voice is negatively affected by <a href="/wiki/Marijuana" class="mw-redirect" title="Marijuana">marijuana</a> smoke, to which he says he is <a href="/wiki/Allergic" class="mw-redirect" title="Allergic">allergic</a>. On 20 May 2015, during a Who concert at <a href="/wiki/Nassau_Coliseum" class="mw-redirect" title="Nassau Coliseum">Nassau Coliseum</a>, he smelled a joint burning and told the smoker to put it out or "the show will be over". The fan obliged, without taking Pete Townshend\'s advice that "the quickest way" to extinguish a joint is "up your fucking arse".<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guitars">Guitars</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuff_from_The_Who_(14165151158).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Collection of Who memorabilia including guitars and clothes" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Stuff_from_The_Who_%2814165151158%29.jpg/220px-Stuff_from_The_Who_%2814165151158%29.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Stuff_from_The_Who_%2814165151158%29.jpg/330px-Stuff_from_The_Who_%2814165151158%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Stuff_from_The_Who_%2814165151158%29.jpg/440px-Stuff_from_The_Who_%2814165151158%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="436" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stuff_from_The_Who_(14165151158).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A selection of instruments used by the Who, including a <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker" title="Rickenbacker">Rickenbacker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gibson_SG_Special" title="Gibson SG Special">Gibson SG Special</a> guitar, and Moon\'s "Pictures of Lily" drum kit from <a href="/wiki/Premier_drums" class="mw-redirect" title="Premier drums">Premier</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Townshend considered himself less technical than guitarists such as <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a> and wanted to stand out visually instead.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200943_319-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200943-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> His playing style evolved from the banjo, favouring <a href="/wiki/Downpicking" title="Downpicking">down strokes</a> and using a combination of the <a href="/wiki/Plectrum" title="Plectrum">plectrum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fingerpicking" class="mw-redirect" title="Fingerpicking">fingerpicking</a>. His rhythm playing frequently used <a href="/wiki/Seventh_chord" title="Seventh chord">seventh chords</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suspended_fourth" class="mw-redirect" title="Suspended fourth">suspended fourths</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-drozdowski_321-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drozdowski-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> and he is associated with the <a href="/wiki/Power_chord" title="Power chord">power chord</a>, an easy-to-finger chord built from the <a href="/wiki/Root_(chord)" title="Root (chord)">root</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fifth_(chord)" title="Fifth (chord)">fifth</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAledort199457_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAledort199457-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> that has since become a fundamental part of the rock guitar vocabulary.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199447_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199447-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup>  Townshend also produced noises by manipulating controls on his guitar and by allowing the instrument to feedback.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199444_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199444-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the group\'s early career, Townshend favoured <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker" title="Rickenbacker">Rickenbacker</a> guitars as they allowed him to fret rhythm guitar chords easily and move the neck back and forwards to create <a href="/wiki/Vibrato" title="Vibrato">vibrato</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> From 1968 to 1973, he favoured a <a href="/wiki/Gibson_SG_Special" title="Gibson SG Special">Gibson SG Special</a> live,<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> and later used customised <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul" title="Gibson Les Paul">Les Pauls</a> in different tunings.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">\n<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Pinball_Wizard.ogg" title="File:Pinball Wizard.ogg">Brief sample from the song "Pinball Wizard"</a></div>\n<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_2" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="18.018684807256" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Pinball_Wizard.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/ea/Pinball_Wizard.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (86 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="86484" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/e/ea/Pinball_Wizard.ogg/Pinball_Wizard.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="205488" /></audio></div></div>\n<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">The opening of "Pinball Wizard" shows Townshend\'s acoustic guitar, with a flamenco influence.</div></div></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In the studio for <i>Who\'s Next</i> and thereafter, Townshend used a 1959 <a href="/wiki/Gretsch_6120" title="Gretsch 6120">Gretsch 6120 Chet Atkins</a> hollow-body guitar, a <a href="/wiki/Fender_Bandmaster" title="Fender Bandmaster">Fender Bandmaster</a> amp and an Edwards <a href="/wiki/Volume_pedal" class="mw-redirect" title="Volume pedal">volume pedal</a>, all gifts from <a href="/wiki/Joe_Walsh" title="Joe Walsh">Joe Walsh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup>  Townshend started his career with an acoustic guitar<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200917_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200917-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and has regularly recorded and written with a <a href="/wiki/Gibson_J-200" title="Gibson J-200">Gibson J-200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bass">Bass</span></h3>\n<p>A distinctive part of the original band\'s sound was Entwistle\'s lead bass playing, while Townshend concentrated on rhythm and chords.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent200924_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent200924-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECampbell2012239_312-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECampbell2012239-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> Entwistle\'s was the first popular use of <a href="/wiki/Rotosound" class="mw-redirect" title="Rotosound">Rotosound</a> strings in 1966, trying to find a piano-like sound.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> His bassline on "Pinball Wizard" was described by Who biographer John Atkins as "a contribution of its own without diminishing the guitar lines";<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAtkins2000116_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAtkins2000116-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> he described his part on "The Real Me" from <i>Quadrophenia</i>, recorded in one take, as "a bass solo with vocals".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnterberger2011203_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnterberger2011203-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> Entwistle\'s basses include a "Frankenstein" assembled from five Fender <a href="/wiki/Fender_Precision_Bass" title="Fender Precision Bass">Precision</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fender_Jazz_Bass" title="Fender Jazz Bass">Jazz</a> basses, and <a href="/wiki/Warwick_(company)" title="Warwick (company)">Warwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alembic" title="Alembic">Alembic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gretsch" title="Gretsch">Gretsch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guild_Guitar_Company" title="Guild Guitar Company">Guild</a> basses.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drums">Drums</span></h3>\n<p>Moon further strengthened the reversal of traditional rock instrumentation by playing lead parts on his drums.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198388_342-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198388-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> His style was at odds with British rock contemporaries such as <a href="/wiki/The_Kinks" title="The Kinks">The Kinks</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Mick_Avory" title="Mick Avory">Mick Avory</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Shadows" title="The Shadows">The Shadows</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Brian_Bennett" title="Brian Bennett">Brian Bennett</a> who did not consider <a href="/wiki/Tom-tom_drum" title="Tom-tom drum">tom-toms</a> necessary for rock music.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998109_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998109-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> Moon used <a href="/wiki/Premier" title="Premier">Premier</a> kits starting in 1966. He avoided the <a href="/wiki/Hi-hat" title="Hi-hat">hi-hat</a>, and concentrated on a mix of tom rolls and <a href="/wiki/Cymbal" title="Cymbal">cymbals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998152_344-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998152-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Jones\' drumming style was in sharp contrast to Moon\'s.  The Who were initially enthusiastic about working with a completely different drummer,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998539_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998539-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> though Townshend later stated, "we\'ve never really been able to replace Keith."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998543_255-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998543-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>  Starkey knew Moon from childhood and Moon gave him his first drum kit. Starkey has been praised for his playing style which echoes Moon\'s without being a copy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998543_255-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998543-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Songwriting">Songwriting</span></h3>\n<p>Townshend focused on writing meaningful lyrics<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh19838_346-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh19838-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> inspired by <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>, whose words dealt with subjects other than boy\xe2\x80\x93girl relationships that were common in rock music; in contrast to Dylan\'s intellectualism, Townshend believed his lyrics should be about things kids could relate to.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199446_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199446-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> Early material focused on the frustration and anxiety shared by mod audiences,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh19838_346-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh19838-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> which Townshend said was a result of "searching for &#91;his&#93; niche".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983118_348-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983118-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> By <i>The Who Sell Out</i>, he began to work narrative and characters into songs,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983282_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983282-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup> which he fully developed by <i>Tommy</i>, including spiritual themes influenced by Baba.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983318_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983318-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> From the mid-1970s onwards, his songs tended to be more personal,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983460_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983460-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> which influenced his decision to go solo.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983518\xe2\x80\x93519_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983518\xe2\x80\x93519-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Entwistle\'s songs, by contrast, typically feature <a href="/wiki/Black_humour" class="mw-redirect" title="Black humour">black humour</a> and darker themes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983252_351-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983252-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> His two contributions to <i>Tommy</i> ("Cousin Kevin" and "Fiddle About") appeared because Townshend did not believe he could write songs as "nasty" as Entwistle\'s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983323_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983323-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_relationships">Personal relationships</span></h2>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:15em;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"We\'re not mates at all."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Roger_Daltrey" title="Roger Daltrey">Roger Daltrey</a>, 1965<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEwbankHildred201228_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEwbankHildred201228-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>The Who are perceived as having had a poor working relationship. In the original band, Sandom had been the peacemaker and settled disputes. Moon, by contrast, was as volatile as Daltrey and Townshend. Entwistle was too passive to become involved in arguments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh198387_353-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh198387-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup> The group established their live reputation and stage show in part out of insecurity and aggression amongst its members<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983122_354-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983122-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup> and Townshend recalled that all decisions had to be made democratically "because we always disagreed".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983140_355-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983140-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:20em;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"I just couldn\'t get through to Pete and Roger. We have absolutely nothing in common apart from music."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Keith_Moon" title="Keith Moon">Keith Moon</a>, 1965<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEwbankHildred201228_352-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEwbankHildred201228-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>The only genuine friendship in the Who during the 1960s was between Entwistle and Moon. The pair enjoyed each other\'s sense of humour and shared a fondness for clubbing. Journalist Richard Green noted a "chemistry of playfullness that would go beyond playfullness".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998126_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998126-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Their relationship diminished somewhat when Entwistle got married in 1967, though they still socialised on tour.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998189_77-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998189-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> When Moon was destroying toilets in hotels, Entwistle confessed he "was standing behind him with the matches".<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The group regularly argued in the press,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983140_355-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983140-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> though Townshend said disputes were amplified in print and the group simply found it difficult to agree on things.<sup id="cite_ref-waddell_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waddell-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> <i>Tommy</i> mutually benefitted Townshend and Daltrey\'s standing in the band because of the former\'s songwriting and the latter\'s stage presence, yet even this did not make them close friends.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983144_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983144-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup> The pair quarrelled, particularly in the mid-1970s, over the group\'s direction.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983426_359-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983426-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup> During his time with the band, Jones was subject to intermittent criticism from Daltrey.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983517_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarsh1983517-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Entwistle\'s death came as a shock to both Townshend and Daltrey, and caused them to re-evaluate their relationship. Townshend has said that he and Daltrey have since become close friends.<sup id="cite_ref-waddell_357-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waddell-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Townshend confirmed their friendship was still strong, adding their acceptance of each other\'s differences "brought us to a really genuine and compassionate relationship, which can only be described as love."<sup id="cite_ref-mojo2015_296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mojo2015-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_and_influence">Legacy and influence</span></h2>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:20em;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"The one thing that disgusts me about the Who is the way they smashed through every door in the uncharted hallway of rock \'n\' roll without leaving much more than some debris for the rest of us to lay claim to."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Eddie_Vedder" title="Eddie Vedder">Eddie Vedder</a><sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>The Who are one of the most influential rock bands of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_vid_362-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_vid-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> Their appearances at Monterey and Woodstock helped give them a reputation as one of the greatest live rock acts<sup id="cite_ref-webb_363-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webb-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup> and they have been credited with originating the "<a href="/wiki/Rock_opera" title="Rock opera">rock opera</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_vid_362-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_vid-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> The band has sold over 100&#160;million records worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The group\'s contributions to rock include the <a href="/wiki/Power_chord" title="Power chord">power chord</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Guitar_showmanship" title="Guitar showmanship">windmill strum</a><sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> and the use of non-musical instrument noise such as feedback.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199444_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199444-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The band influenced fashion from their earliest days with their embrace of <a href="/wiki/Pop_art" title="Pop art">pop art</a><sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> and the use of the <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">Union Jack</a> for clothing.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup>  The guitar-smashing incident at the Railway Hotel in 1964 is one of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine\'s "50&#160;Moments That Changed the History of Rock \'n\' Roll".<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a> began to use feedback from their early shows in 1966, inspired by the Who, whom they considered a formative influence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteley200327_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteley200327-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after arriving in London in 1966, <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a> visited Marshall\'s music shop demanding an amp setup like Townshend\'s<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199446_347-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199446-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> and manipulated electronic noises in ways that Townshend had pioneered.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199444_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiPerna199444-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> were fans and socialised with Moon in particular during the mid-1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998127_371-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998127-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup> In 1965, <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a> said the Who "are the most exciting thing around"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998127_371-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFletcher1998127-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup> and was inspired to write "<a href="/wiki/Helter_Skelter_(song)" title="Helter Skelter (song)">Helter Skelter</a>" in the group\'s "heavy" style;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald1997261_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald1997261-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a> borrowed the acoustic guitar style in "Pinball Wizard" for "<a href="/wiki/Polythene_Pam" title="Polythene Pam">Polythene Pam</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald1997319_373-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald1997319-373">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The loud volume of the band\'s live show influenced the approach of hard rock and <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKnowles2013140_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKnowles2013140-374">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Proto_punk" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto punk">Proto punk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> bands such as the <a href="/wiki/MC5" title="MC5">MC5</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Stooges" title="The Stooges">the Stooges</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Ramones" title="Ramones">Ramones</a><sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup> the Sex Pistols,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009396_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeillKent2009396-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Clash" title="The Clash">the Clash</a><sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a> cite the Who as an influence.<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup> The Who inspired <a href="/wiki/Mod_revival" title="Mod revival">mod revival</a> bands, particularly <a href="/wiki/The_Jam" title="The Jam">the Jam</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup> which helped other groups influenced by the Who become popular.<sup id="cite_ref-webb_363-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webb-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup> The Who influenced hard rock bands such as <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N&#39; Roses">Guns N\' Roses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup> In the mid-1990s, <a href="/wiki/Britpop" title="Britpop">Britpop</a> bands such as <a href="/wiki/Blur_(band)" title="Blur (band)">Blur</a><sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Oasis_(band)" title="Oasis (band)">Oasis</a> were influenced by the Who.<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup> The Who have also influenced <a href="/wiki/Pop_punk" title="Pop punk">pop punk</a> band <a href="/wiki/Panic!_at_the_Disco" title="Panic! at the Disco">Panic! at the Disco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Who have inspired many tribute bands; Daltrey has endorsed <a href="/wiki/The_Whodlums" title="The Whodlums">the Whodlums</a>, who raise money for the <a href="/wiki/Teenage_Cancer_Trust" title="Teenage Cancer Trust">Teenage Cancer Trust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup> Many bands have covered Who songs; <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>\'s version of "Pinball Wizard" reached No.&#160;7 in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>\n<p>During the Who\'s hiatuses in the 1980s and 90s, Townshend developed his skills as a music publisher to be financially successful from the Who without recording or touring. He countered criticism of "selling out" by saying that licensing the songs to other media allows a wider exposure and widens the group\'s appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-waddell_357-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waddell-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The American forensic drama <i>CSI</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/CSI:_Crime_Scene_Investigation" title="CSI: Crime Scene Investigation">CSI: Crime Scene Investigation</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/CSI:_Miami" title="CSI: Miami">CSI: Miami</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/CSI:_NY" title="CSI: NY">CSI: NY</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/CSI:_Cyber" title="CSI: Cyber">CSI: Cyber</a></i>) feature Who songs as theme music, "<a href="/wiki/Who_Are_You_(song)" title="Who Are You (song)">Who Are You</a>", "Won\'t Get Fooled Again", "Baba O\'Riley" and "I Can See for Miles" respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup> The group\'s songs have featured in other popular TV series such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Top_Gear_(2002_TV_series)" title="Top Gear (2002 TV series)">Top Gear</a></i>, which had an episode where the presenters were tasked with being roadies for the band.<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">&#91;391&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rock-orientated films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Almost_Famous" title="Almost Famous">Almost Famous</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">&#91;392&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/School_of_Rock" title="School of Rock">School of Rock</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">&#91;393&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tenacious_D_in_the_Pick_of_Destiny" class="mw-redirect" title="Tenacious D in the Pick of Destiny">Tenacious D in the Pick of Destiny</a></i> refer to the band and feature their songs,<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">&#91;394&#93;</a></sup> and other films have used the band\'s material in their soundtracks, including <i><a href="/wiki/Apollo_13_(film)" title="Apollo 13 (film)">Apollo 13</a></i> (which used "I Can See For Miles")<sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Austin_Powers:_The_Spy_Who_Shagged_Me" title="Austin Powers: The Spy Who Shagged Me">Austin Powers: The Spy Who Shagged Me</a></i> (which used a take of "My Generation" recorded for the BBC).<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup> Several of the band\'s tracks have appeared in the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band_(video_game)" title="Rock Band (video game)">Rock Band</a></i> and its sequels.<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_The_Who" title="List of awards and nominations received by The Who">List of awards and nominations received by The Who</a></div>\n<p>The Who have received many awards and accolades from the music industry for their recordings and their influence. They received a Lifetime Achievement Award from the British Phonographic Industry in 1988,<sup id="cite_ref-BPI_398-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPI-398">&#91;398&#93;</a></sup> and from the Grammy Foundation in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_399-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy-399">&#91;399&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The band were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 1990 where their display describes them as "prime contenders, in the minds of many, for the title of World\'s Greatest Rock Band",<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_Montgomery_400-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_Montgomery-400">&#91;400&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="UK Music Hall of Fame">UK Music Hall of Fame</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-402">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup> Seven of the group\'s albums appeared on <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time" title="Rolling Stone&#39;s 500 Greatest Albums of All Time"><i>Rolling Stone</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s 500&#160;Greatest Albums of All Time</a> in 2003, more than any act except <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">the Rolling Stones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-403" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-403">&#91;403&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Band_members">Band members</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article:
